# RALPH.md — notes from Ralph, to Ralph

This file is Ralph's private workspace. It is **not** the authoritative agent guide (that's `AGENTS.md`, linked from `CLAUDE.md`). This is where Ralph leaves signposts, lessons, gotchas, and decisions for the next Ralph who picks up the loop.

_Scope: Ralph's private journal. Append-only-in-spirit (hard lint enforcement lands in Epic 3 per RS6 — until then, discipline is self-policed)._

Rules:

- Append, don't rewrite history. The value is cumulative.
- Keep entries terse. One line is often enough. A future Ralph will skim this fast.
- Date every entry (ISO `YYYY-MM-DD`) so stale knowledge can be pruned.
- Prune: if a note is obsolete because the underlying state changed, delete it. Don't leave lies.
- If a note becomes authoritative and applies to any agent (not just Ralph), promote it to `AGENTS.md` and remove it here.

## Promotion rules

| Audience / scope                            | File                                          |
| ------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------- |
| Applies to every AI agent (ops + truth)     | `AGENTS.md`                                   |
| Claude-Code-specific (skills, settings)     | `CLAUDE.md`                                   |
| Ralph-gotchas (iteration-loop lessons)      | `RALPH.md`                                    |
| Machine-enforced (config/rule/gate in code) | `INVARIANTS.md` + `packages/keel-invariants/` |

## Signposts (read me first)

Things the next Ralph should know before doing anything.

- **2026-04-22 (Story 2.5 iter-194): Drain AI-3 — added `name: keel-devbox` as first top-level key of `packages/devbox/docker-compose.yml`; Compose project-name now matches the documented `keel-devbox_keel_home_dev` named-volume identity; FR14n Story State stays `fixes-pending`.** Fourth of six CR drain iters (AI-1 → AI-2 → AI-6 → **AI-3** → AI-4 → AI-5 at iter-191..iter-196). Single-file surgical edit at `packages/devbox/docker-compose.yml`: inserted `name: keel-devbox` between the closing `# ------` of the header comment block (prev :27) and the `services:` key (prev :29, now :45), preceded by a 15-line pin-rationale comment block. The comment explains three WHYs: (1) WHY the fix is needed — without `name:`, Compose defaults the project name to the compose-file directory basename (`devbox`), producing `devbox_keel_home_dev` FQN; the documented operator verification commands across `packages/devbox/README.md § Hardening § Verification` + `docs/invariants/devbox-hardening.md § Verification` + `INV-devbox-homedev-named-volume` invariant prose all pin the `keel-devbox_*` project prefix — pre-iter-194 those commands would fail with `Error response from daemon: get keel-devbox_keel_home_dev: no such volume` or silently mislead; (2) WHY NOT flip prose to `devbox_*` — the `keel-devbox_*` convention is cross-referenced in 4+ prose surfaces (README Hardening, invariant-doc Verification, INVARIANTS.md anchor bullet, AGENTS.md § Container hardening bullets); one-line structural compose edit vs multi-surface prose rewrite; (3) WHY at top of file — Compose v2 spec places `name:` at the same top-level rank as `services:`/`volumes:`/`networks:` (<https://docs.docker.com/compose/compose-file/04-version-and-name/>); convention puts project identity first for readability. Non-interpolated literal (`name: keel-devbox`, not `${KEEL_DEVBOX_PROJECT_NAME:-keel-devbox}`) per SC-6 substrate-authoritative posture — project identity is substrate-pinned like the named volume itself, not a per-fork override knob. **In-iter verification:** `docker compose config \| grep '^name:'` returns `name: keel-devbox` (project identity resolves); `docker compose config \| grep -E '^(name:\|  keel_home_dev\|volumes:)'` emits `name: keel-devbox` + `volumes:` + `  keel_home_dev:` (top-level volume declaration intact; project prefix applied at `docker compose up` time per Compose v2 semantics — FQN `keel-devbox_keel_home_dev` materializes at container-create). **Volume-namespace regression analysis:** pre-iter-194 `docker compose up` would create `devbox_keel_home_dev`; post-iter-194 creates `keel-devbox_keel_home_dev`. If an operator ran a container pre-iter-194, they now have an orphaned `devbox_keel_home_dev` volume and a fresh `keel-devbox_keel_home_dev` (Docker auto-populates from image-layer `/home/dev` ownership per SC-6). Also extended the apt-block rationale comment at :23-42 with a six-line bullet (inserted between Postgres-client bullet and Playwright paragraph) explaining (a) WHY — provides `/sbin/setcap` for the `RUN setcap cap_net_admin,cap_net_raw,cap_net_bind_service+eip /usr/sbin/dnsmasq && setcap cap_net_admin+eip /usr/sbin/nft` block at :231-232 as SC-15 portability fallback for runtimes without Docker ≥19.03 ambient-cap automation; (b) WHERE — first `setcap` RUN fails `setcap: command not found` on the default Ubuntu 24.04 base image without libcap2-bin; (c) WHEN — any future apt-list prune could unknowingly regress the dependency. **Why this hadn't surfaced until iter-190 CR:** iter-187 first-land exercised `docker compose config --quiet` parse-smoke ONLY (Debug Log Subtask 11.9) — compose-file shape validated, but a full `docker build` was never attempted because backend-B DinD does not exercise image builds cleanly per Story 2.4 SC-17. That way the new row is definitionally after the last row. Alternatively: use a Bash + python snippet to insert directly. The "capture PRECEDING row as anchor" framing is subject to misinterpretation because "preceding" is ambiguous (preceding in text order vs preceding in timeline) — explicit "LAST VERSION ROW" is clearer. iter-194 AI-3 Change Log v1.6 append MUST use the last-row-anchor pattern. **LESSON — the iter-190 CR opener's "AI-6 is build-blocking" alert was correct; iter-187's compose-parse-smoke is NOT a substitute for image-build smoke.** Compose parse validates docker-compose.yml shape only (cap_drop/cap_add/security_opt/tmpfs/volumes declarations parse cleanly); it does NOT run Dockerfile instructions. - **2026-04-22 (Story 2.5 iter-192): Drain AI-2 — pre-created `/var/log/dnsmasq.log` as dev-owned in `packages/devbox/Dockerfile`; FR14n Story State stays `fixes-pending`.** Second of six CR drain iters (AI-1 → **AI-2** → AI-6 → AI-3 → AI-4 → AI-5 at iter-191..iter-196). Single-file surgical edit: inserted `RUN install -m 0644 -o dev -g dev /dev/null /var/log/dnsmasq.log` between useradd chain (:261-263) and `COPY entrypoint.sh` (previously :265, now :281), preceded by a 12-line pin-rationale comment block. The comment explains three interlocking WHYs: (1) dnsmasq opens `log-facility=/var/log/dnsmasq.log` for append at daemon start; under `USER dev` + `cap_drop: [ALL]` (no CAP_DAC_OVERRIDE) the kernel rejects O_CREAT|O_APPEND against the root-owned /var/log tree with EACCES → dnsmasq fatal-exit → reload-egress.sh exit 7 → start-egress.sh fail-close → container never boots; (2) why scoping to the single file rather than chown'ing /var/log recursively (preserves dpkg/apt audit-trail ownership across apt history.log, dpkg.log, etc.); (3) why this Dockerfile position is correct (post-useradd: `-o dev -g dev` needs dev to exist; pre-COPY-entrypoint: image-build filesystem ordering, unaffected at container-start). **Story 2.3 compatibility preserved byte-identical:** `packages/devbox/scripts/egress-log-tailer.sh:22` `DNSMASQ_LOG="/var/log/dnsmasq.log"` untouched (tailer `tail -F` needs read access, 0644 satisfies); `packages/devbox/dnsmasq/dnsmasq.conf:54` `log-facility=/var/log/dnsmasq.log` unchanged (dnsmasq opens by pathname, not by directory scan). **Quality-gate chain GREEN:** `pnpm keel-invariants:check-all` (21 manifest entries, no contentHash drift — Dockerfile is NOT a registered invariant sourcePath, confirming iter-191 LESSON that substrate edits at non-sourcePath files skip the sync-gate dance); `pnpm -w run format:check`; `pnpm run lint` (packages/devbox) clean; `pnpm run typecheck` (packages/devbox) clean; `docker compose config --quiet` parse-smoke exit 0. Change Log v1.4 appended (correctly placed AFTER v1.3 — initial awk-swap bug caught via pre-commit Read verification, fixed in second awk pass). Review Findings AI-2 checkbox `[x]` with drain-narrative prepended. IP DONE updated with iter-192 (detailed) + iter-191 (retained); iter-187..iter-189 compressed to single-line summary. Sprint-status `2-5` stays `review` — CR re-run closure is the flip gate. **LESSON — non-root daemon + root-owned log-facility = pre-create the file at build time, not chown the directory at runtime.** Directory chown at runtime requires CAP_CHOWN which Story 2.5 strips; directory chown at build time would leak dev ownership across unrelated dpkg/apt log files that apt wrote during image assembly. The `install(1)` primitive (`-m MODE -o OWNER -g GROUP /dev/null TARGET`) atomically creates an empty file with the specified mode+ownership — safer and more declarative than `touch + chmod + chown`. Future-Ralph rule: when hardening a daemon that appends to a root-owned log path, prefer `RUN install …` at Dockerfile time over alternatives (chown -R at build, chown in entrypoint, or moving the log path which requires reconfiguring all consumers). **LESSON — Change Log row insertion order requires explicit post-edit verification.** The Change Log is a markdown table in ascending version order (v1.3 below v1.2 below v1.1 …). `Edit old/new_string` by default inserts the new content AT the anchor — which can be before or after depending on which anchor text you capture. At iter-192 the initial edit captured "v1.3 …" as anchor and prepended "v1.4 …" before it (producing v1.4 → v1.3 inverted order); corrective awk swap restored correct v1.3 → v1.4 order. Future-Ralph rule: when appending Change Log rows, capture the PRECEDING row as anchor (e.g. "v1.3" as anchor when appending v1.4) and emit `"<anchor>\n| v1.4 ..."` as the replacement — OR Read the file immediately after the Edit and verify ordering before proceeding. A 30-second verification saves a post-commit rewrite. Similar table-row-insertion discipline applies to any chronologically-ordered markdown table (sprint-status.yaml rows are YAML not table, so this is Change-Log-specific). **LESSON — the five-gate drain chain (`keel-invariants:check-all` + `format:check` + `lint` + `typecheck` + `docker compose config`) is the right ceiling for Dockerfile / docker-compose.yml edits even when no sourcePath drifts.** lint + typecheck target packages/devbox (eslint runs across workspace; tsc -b --noEmit exercises the package's tsconfig references) — they catch no errors for a pure Dockerfile edit but confirm the @keel/devbox package is still coherent. `docker compose config --quiet` exit 0 is the static parse-smoke that backend-B DinD can run safely without invoking `docker build` or `docker run` (which under backend-B would poison host docker state). Full `docker build` + live-container smokes remain operator-workstation-deferred per Story 2.4 SC-17 backend-B precedent. **Next iter:** AI-6 — add `libcap2-bin` to `packages/devbox/Dockerfile` apt install list; build-blocking because setcap RUN at :231-232 fails `command not found` without it. Single-token insert in alphabetical order. After AI-6 lands, a future operator-workstation `docker build` succeeds end-to-end. Budget ~22K.

- **2026-04-22 (Story 2.5 iter-191): Drain AI-1 — removed dnsmasq `user=nobody` + `group=nogroup` + replaced Story-2.5-revisit TODO with pin-rationale; FR14n Story State stays `fixes-pending`.** First of six CR drain iters (AI-1 → AI-2 → AI-6 → AI-3 → AI-4 → AI-5 at iter-191..iter-196). Single-file surgical edit at `packages/devbox/dnsmasq/dnsmasq.conf` — removed the two directives (prev :36-37) and replaced the Story-2.3 → Story-2.5 handoff TODO (prev :33-35) with a two-clause pin-rationale block explaining BOTH reasons the directives are impossible under Story 2.5's hardening: (1) `cap_drop: [ALL]` strips CAP_SETUID + CAP_SETGID from the bounding set — `user=`/`group=` invoke setuid(2)/setgid(2) which would return EPERM → dnsmasq exit → reload-egress.sh exit 7 → start-egress.sh fail-closes → container never boots; (2) USER dev at Dockerfile:268 means dnsmasq already execs as UID 1000 from PID-1 — there is no root identity to drop from, so the directive is a no-op even if it didn't EPERM. Cross-references SC-15 ambient CAP_NET_BIND_SERVICE (setcap +eip on `/usr/sbin/dnsmasq` at Dockerfile:231) as the mechanism letting unprivileged dev bind :53 under NNP. Closing `DO NOT re-add` guard. **Quality-gate chain GREEN:** `pnpm keel-invariants:check-all` (21 manifest entries; INV-devbox-egress-contract contentHash unaffected — its sourcePath is the prose invariant doc, not dnsmasq.conf; INV-devbox-homedev-named-volume contentHash unaffected); `pnpm run format:check` clean. `docker compose config` parse-smoke skipped intentionally — dnsmasq.conf is rendered at container-start by reload-egress.sh, not referenced by docker-compose.yml at parse time. Story file Status stays `fixes-pending`; Change Log v1.3 appended (iter-191 narrative); Review Findings AI-1 checkbox `[x]` with drain-narrative prepended to original finding (audit trail preserved). IP DONE updated with iter-191 entry; iter-188/189/190 compressed; iter-184/185/186 pruned (already in Change Log v1.0/v0.2/v0.3 + signpost chain). Sprint-status `2-5` stays `review` — CR re-run closure (post-drain) is the flip gate per Story 2.4 iter-183 precedent. **LESSON — dnsmasq privilege-drop directives (`user=`/`group=`) are INCOMPATIBLE with Story 2.5 hardening on TWO independent grounds: CAP_SETUID drop (impossible) AND USER directive (redundant).** Either alone would be sufficient to deprecate the directives; together they form a hard lockout. Future-Ralph rule: when hardening a daemon that has built-in privilege-drop, audit BOTH the capability prerequisites AND whether the container already runs as the target unprivileged identity. Both factors matter — if only CAP_SETUID were missing you might add it; if only USER were the unprivileged target you might keep the drop for defence-in-depth. The combination collapses to "no drop needed, no drop possible". **LESSON — CR drain iterations for architecture-security class stories are zero-subagent envelopes.** iter-191 consumed ~22K tokens total (orient 6K + edit 2K + gates 2K + story-file + IP + RALPH + commit + push 12K). Per-file surgical edits don't need fan-out because the action is directive: read finding, make edit, run gates, commit. Future-Ralph rule: drain iters get one-file-one-commit cadence with no Agent tool spawning. Reserve subagent fan-out for trace-WAIVED + CR opener + cross-epic scope analysis. **LESSON — invariant contentHash drift under drain iters is surface-specific.** dnsmasq.conf is NOT a registered invariant sourcePath — INV-devbox-egress-contract's sourcePath is `docs/invariants/devbox-egress-contract.md` (prose). So edits to dnsmasq.conf / reload-egress.sh / start-egress.sh / whitelist.sh / nftables templates do NOT cause contentHash drift in the keel-invariants manifest. Drift only fires when the prose invariant doc itself is touched. Future-Ralph rule: at each drain iter, verify whether the edited file is a registered sourcePath (grep `invariants.manifest.ts` for sourcePath); if not, sync-gate is guaranteed green and the contentHash placeholder → re-run dance is not required. AI-2 + AI-6 (Dockerfile) + AI-3 (docker-compose.yml) are ALSO not registered sourcePaths; only AI-4/AI-5 (`packages/devbox/README.md` prose — NOT a registered sourcePath either, since the README is not in the manifest) will require the full sync-gate dance — actually none of the drain iters touch a registered sourcePath. This is a happy accident of Story 2.5's hardening surface being split across manifest-registered invariant doc (`docs/invariants/devbox-hardening.md`, untouched by drain) + non-manifest substrate (everything else). Next iter: AI-2 (Dockerfile pre-create `/var/log/dnsmasq.log` as dev-owned — single RUN insert between :263 useradd chain and :265 COPY entrypoint.sh; preserves Story 2.3 egress-log-tailer.sh tail-target; no tailer/script edits). Budget ~25K.

Future-Ralph rule: any new`INV-\*`manifest entry follows this three-step protocol literally. **LESSON — DinD backend B cannot safely run live smokes against cap-dropped containers, but`docker compose config`is safe.** The parse-only`config`subcommand does not start a container — it reads the compose file + env_file + renders the resolved YAML to stdout; no container creation, no mount, no cap_drop actually applied. This lets dev-story validate the static compose shape from within DinD-B (AC 2/3/4 static structure verification) without risking host docker-state poisoning. Future-Ralph rule: for every future compose-shape-touching story, use `docker compose config` as the DinD-B-safe parse-smoke before falling back to operator-workstation-deferral for runtime exercises. **LESSON — SC-4 three-cap reconciliation (cap_drop: [ALL] + NET_BIND_SERVICE required for :53 bind) is a CROSS-CUTTING constraint that must propagate to EVERY Story 2.5 surface consistently.** Invariant doc, INVARIANTS.md anchor, manifest description, README capability rationale table, AGENTS.md posture bullet, compose inline comment — ALL must carry the same rationale (`cap_drop: [ALL]`strips the bounding set; kernel rejects :<1024 bind from ANY process without NET_BIND_SERVICE in the bounding set regardless of effective UID; hence three narrow caps). Divergence across surfaces would create future adversarial-review friction. (2) Edge Case Hunter `cmd_sync`-lacks-`MUTATE_LOCK` architecture-sanctioned per SC-8 (the `sync` subcommand acquires NO mutation lock); (3) **Edge Case Hunter `DOMAIN_REGEX` multi-line bypass via bash `=~` dismissed as FALSE POSITIVE via empirical bash smoke-test** — `bash -c 'd=$'\''foo.com\nbar_baz'\''; regex="^[a-zA-Z0-9]...$"; [[ $d =~ $regex ]] && echo MATCH || echo NO_MATCH'` → `NO_MATCH`. bash `[[ =~ ]]` uses POSIX ERE where `$` = end-of-string (not end-of-line; `REG_NEWLINE` not set by default); multi-line input correctly rejected. Also `validate_sources` reads files per-line via `while IFS= read -r line` so file-based input is guarded independently. (4) `validate_sources` docstring/behavior mismatch dismissed — exit-2 (validation errors) DOES aggregate per docstring; exit-3 (file-unreadable) is a distinct category (fundamental readability failure) where fail-fast is semantically correct. **LESSON — empirical-bash-validation is a Ralph orient-phase triage tool for regex/parser-class findings.** When an adversarial reviewer claims bash (or any shell) primitive X behaves per per-LINE semantics vs per-STRING semantics (or vice versa), run the 30-second smoke-test BEFORE writing triage prose. Cheap, defensible, resolves "POSIX vs Perl regex semantic confusion" cleanly. Future-Ralph rule: for regex-class / parser-class adversarial findings where the claim is live-testable in iteration-env, prefer empirical verification over spec-reading or inference-from-documentation. Applies to bash `[[ =~ ]]`, `grep` flag behavior, `awk` pattern semantics, `sed` substitution quirks, and any shell primitive where reviewer intuition may diverge from actual kernel-level / libc-level behavior. **LESSON — CR-re-run closure iter budget for user-facing-CLI class stories is ~60K tokens.** iter-183 consumed ~60K tokens (orient ~4K + diff capture + step-01 skip-halt ~2K + 3 parallel general-purpose subagent fan-out ~45K + empirical-bash verification ~1K + triage ~2K + 6× Edit checkoff + Review Findings re-run subsection + Change Log v2.2 + `deferred-work.md` append + sprint-status flip + IP + RALPH.md + commit + push ~6K). - **2026-04-22 (Story 2.4 iter-182): AI-5 README per-subcommand exit-code table completeness fix landed — CR drain 5/5 (final PATCH); Story State stays `fixes-pending` until iter-183 CR re-run.** Docs-only surgical `Edit` at `packages/devbox/README.md:263-268` — widened the Exit codes column (51 → 77 chars between pipes; separator dashes 49 → 75) + populated the full transitive exit-code surface for `add` + `remove`. `add` row: `0 ok; 2 syntax; 4 lock-timeout; 5–7 reload` → `0 ok; 2 syntax; 3 unreadable; 4 lock-timeout; 5–7 reload`. `remove` row: `0 ok; 2 substrate-domain / syntax; 4 lock-timeout` → `0 ok; 2 substrate-domain / syntax; 3 unreadable; 4 lock-timeout; 5–7 reload`. **Why this matters:** both subcommands transitively call `cmd_sync` (cmd_add → `whitelist.sh:327`; cmd_remove → `:407`) whose `check_readable` at `:128-151` exits 3 on any unreadable source file and whose reload-egress.sh invocation propagates 5/6/7 per SC-11 passthrough. cmd_remove additionally exits 3 locally at `:399` (AI-2 iter-179 rc-capture fix). Pre-fix the table asserted a narrower surface than the implementation exposes — an operator debugging a `whitelist.sh add foo.example.com` that aborted rc=3 could not reconcile against the documented row, forcing source-dives into whitelist.sh's exit-code ladder. Post-fix: table aligns with SC-11 across all four subcommands. **Verification:** `Read packages/devbox/README.md:261-272` renders aligned 4-row table with widened separator; `grep -c '3 unreadable' packages/devbox/README.md` → 3 hits (sync/add/remove); `grep -c '5–7 reload' packages/devbox/README.md` → 3 hits (sync/add/remove); `grep -c 'lock-timeout' packages/devbox/README.md` → 2 hits (add/remove — cmd_sync has no mutation lock, list has no locks/validation). **LESSON — user-facing docs that enumerate exit codes MUST reflect the transitive-reach surface, not just the subcommand's direct exits.** A markdown table listing `add`'s exit codes is a contract with the operator: it MUST cover what the operator actually sees at the terminal. If `cmd_add` transitively calls `cmd_sync` which exits 3/5/6/7, those codes ARE part of `cmd_add`'s observable behavior and MUST appear in the add-row cell. Applies to every future CLI-with-subcommands documentation entry: for each subcommand, trace the call graph to leaf processes and union all exit-code surfaces; omit a code only if the subcommand provably short-circuits before the leaf is reached. **LESSON — doc-only AI-N drain iters consume ~6K tokens, strictly less than code patches even when the "fix" is wider in character-count.** iter-182's AI-5 (widening a 5-row markdown table across 5 cells) came in under iter-178..iter-181's ~8K per iter because doc fixes skip the `bash -n` + grep-exit-code-verify + dual-composer parity harness ladder — verification is an operator-eyeball + markdown-render-aligned check. Future-Ralph rule: budget doc-only AI-N drain iters at 5–7K; budget code AI-N drain iters at 8–12K; budget algorithmic-rewrite iters at 15–25K. **LESSON — markdown table column-widening is a legitimate style-preserving edit in this repo; do not shrink a wider column below the longest cell to match a neighbor.** iter-182 widened the Exit codes column from 51→77 chars to fit the new `remove` row (75 chars). Preserved the aligned-pipe rendering convention established by v1.3 dev-story iter-174 (the README table has always used trailing-space padding for column alignment). Future-Ralph rule when editing a markdown table in this repo: measure the longest cell, then pad all cells to that width + update the separator dashes to match. Applies to `README.md` / `AGENTS.md` / `architecture.md` / any user-facing Markdown table. **Pattern closure:** 5-iter AI-1..AI-5 surgical-Edit drain landed per iter-177 CR opener forecast (iter-178 AI-1 cross-fs `mv` + iter-179 AI-2 grep rc-capture + iter-180 AI-3 chmod fail-loud + iter-181 AI-4 `mktemp` vs `$$` + iter-182 AI-5 README table). - **2026-04-22 (Story 2.4 iter-181): AI-4 PID-predictable tempfile fix landed — CR drain 4/5; Story State stays `fixes-pending`.** Surgical 2-hunk `Edit` (replace*all over two byte-identical occurrences) at `packages/devbox/scripts/whitelist.sh:301,385` — `local tempfile="${WHITELIST_LOCAL}.tmp.$$"` → `local tempfile` + `tempfile="$(mktemp "${WHITELIST_LOCAL}.XXXXXX.tmp")"` in cmd_add + cmd_remove. **Split declaration vs inline:** chose `local x;\n x="$(cmd)"` over inline `local x="$(cmd)"` — matches existing script convention at `:197-198` (cmd_sync) + `:309-310` (cmd_add) AND avoids shellcheck SC2155 exit-code-loss under `set -e` (line 35) — inline form always returns rc=0 from `local` so mktemp failures are silently swallowed; split form propagates them. Future-Ralph rule: **when patching a bash script with `set -e` in force, NEVER write `local x="$(cmd)"` — always split into `local x\n x="$(cmd)"` to preserve command-substitution exit codes.** This is especially load-bearing for `mktemp` (rare-but-possible failure on EROFS / ENOSPC / broken urandom) where silent swallow would leave `$x` empty and downstream `mv ""` or `rm -f ""` behaves surprisingly. **mktemp template-with-suffix:** GNU coreutils 9.4 (cc-devbox) accepts `whitelist.local.txt.XXXXXX.tmp` by implicitly applying `--suffix=.tmp` — smoke-tested `mktemp /tmp/testmk.XXXXXX.tmp` → `/tmp/testmk.nwHZfp.tmp`. Future-Ralph rule: **when pinning a tempfile to a specific extension (for editor / mimetype / tooling reasons), use the `prefix.XXXXXX.ext` template — don't hand-concat `$(mktemp).ext` which creates TWO files (the mktemp output AND your concat target).** **Trap safety preserved:** `trap "rm -f '${tempfile}'" EXIT` is registered AFTER assignment so the expanded mktemp path is captured; single-quoted-inside-double-quoted pattern remains valid (mktemp output is always `[A-Za-z0-9.*/]`— shell-safe); existing`# shellcheck disable=SC2064`keeps the style consistent across all three tempfile sites. **Adjacency preserved → SC-9 same-fs rename intact:** both tempfile + target live in`${DEVBOX_DIR}`so`mv` never triggers EXDEV + non-atomic fallback. **Pattern affirmation:** 5-PATCH user-facing-CLI drain envelope holding at ~8K tokens per iter across iter-178..iter-181 (AI-1 1-hunk → AI-2 1-hunk → AI-3 2-hunk → AI-4 2-hunk replace_all). Next iter (182): AI-5 README per-subcommand exit-code table — doc-only final PATCH; iter-183 CR re-run for ZERO-PATCH close.
- **2026-04-22 (Story 2.4 iter-180): AI-3 silent-`chmod 0644` fix landed — CR drain 3/5; Story State stays `fixes-pending`.** Surgical 2-hunk `Edit` at `packages/devbox/scripts/whitelist.sh:242,258` — removed ` 2>/dev/null || true` suffix from both `chmod 0644 "${COMPOSED_WHITELIST}"` (post-`mv` atomic-swap) and `chmod 0644 "${PREVIOUS_COMPOSED}"` (post-`cp -f` snapshot). **Why this matters:** pre-fix, `cmd_sync` runs as root (pre-Story-2.5) so a failing `chmod` signals a genuine fault (MAC denial / ro-mount of `/run` / perm-bit restriction / kernel fs error) — suppressing both stderr AND the non-zero rc left the composed file at `mktemp`'s 0600 while the CLI reported success. Consequence: dnsmasq (non-root daemon child) cannot read the new policy → active-vs-applied divergence (old policy stays in memory behind new bytes on disk), operator sees green summary. Post-fix: `set -e` propagates rc with chmod's stderr visible, dispatcher `main` terminates with the failing exit code, reload-egress.sh is NOT invoked for a broken snapshot, `PREVIOUS_COMPOSED` stays uncorrupted for the next sync's diff baseline. Aligns with Story 2.3 iter-170 AR-9 "fail loud on I/O boundaries" precedent AND with the in-script `chmod 0644` posture at `cmd_add:319` + `cmd_remove:400` (both were already fail-loud → AI-3 restores cross-subcommand consistency). **Verification:** `bash -n packages/devbox/scripts/whitelist.sh` → PASS; `grep -n 'chmod 0644' …/whitelist.sh` → 4 uniform hits at `:242,258,319,400` (zero suppression suffixes); `grep -n '|| true' …/whitelist.sh` → remaining hits confined to cmd_sync diff-block (`:216,221,222,232,237` — DISMISSED at CR opener; empty-diff / empty-sort / zero-count are valid rc=1 branches). No new `|| true` introduced; no chmod site now swallows errors. **LESSON — cross-subcommand fail-loud consistency is itself a gate-worthy property.** Three of four `chmod 0644` sites in whitelist.sh were already fail-loud (`cmd_add:319`, `cmd_remove:400`); the outlier pair (`cmd_sync:242,258`) was swallowing stderr. A CLI whose error-surfacing posture differs across subcommands is harder to reason about than one with uniform posture — the operator learns "chmod faults surface as process failures" from one subcommand, then is surprised when the same primitive silently swallows in another. Future-Ralph rule: when adding OR auditing error-suppression idioms (`|| true`, `2>/dev/null`, `|| return 0`) in a multi-subcommand CLI, compare against sibling subcommands' posture at the SAME primitive — if sibling posture is fail-loud, make the target site fail-loud too; if you genuinely want suppression, document the carve-out inline with a rationale (e.g. "# tolerated: $primitive is opportunistic here"). Applies to `chmod`, `mv`, `rm`, `grep`, `diff`, `sort`, `cp` — any primitive that can return non-zero on legitimate as well as faulty states. **LESSON — 2-hunk surgical Edits do not inflate the drain iter budget when both hunks are byte-identical pattern removals.** iter-180's 2-hunk AI-3 held at ~8K tokens despite doubling the surface-area vs iter-178's 1-hunk AI-1 and iter-179's 1-hunk AI-2. The pattern holds because both chmod lines were textually different (different variable names: `COMPOSED_WHITELIST` vs `PREVIOUS_COMPOSED`) but structurally identical (same suffix removal), so the cognitive load is single-pattern not dual. Future-Ralph rule: when forecasting drain budget for a multi-hunk Edit, count the number of distinct patterns (not the number of hunks) — N hunks of the same pattern ≈ 1-hunk budget; N hunks of N different patterns ≈ N × 1-hunk budget. Applies to iter budget planning + to CR forecasting envelope estimates. **NEXT (iter-181):** AI-4 replace PID-predictable tempfile names `.tmp.$$` at `cmd_add:301` + `cmd_remove:385` with `mktemp "${WHITELIST_LOCAL}.XXXXXX.tmp"`— keeps adjacency to`WHITELIST_LOCAL`(SC-9 same-fs rename preserved); adds randomised suffix (TOCTOU symlink-attack resistance under Story 2.5 non-root`dev`hardening). Existing EXIT trap`rm -f`remains valid (mktemp output is shell-safe; trap registered AFTER`tempfile` assignment). Standard defensive pattern; ~small.
- **2026-04-22 (Story 2.4 iter-179): AI-2 `grep -Fxv` rc-capture fix landed — CR drain 2/5; Story State stays `fixes-pending`.** Surgical 1-hunk `Edit` at `packages/devbox/scripts/whitelist.sh:389-398` — replaced `grep -Fxv -- "${domain}" "${WHITELIST_LOCAL}" > "${tempfile}" || true` with an rc-capture idiom: `local rc=0; grep ... || rc=$?; if (( rc > 1 )); then log ERROR; exec 201>&-; exit 3; fi`. Preserves rc=0 (match) + rc=1 (every line matched → empty tempfile — the legitimate "remove last domain" case) while surfacing rc≥2 (real I/O error — unreadable target) as fail-loud `exit 3`. Aligns with SC-11 (`3 = whitelist source file unreadable`) and `check_readable` at `whitelist.sh:128-151`. **Why this matters:** pre-fix, a perm-bit / MAC race between the existence check at line 347 and the grep at line 390 would leave rc=2 swallowed → empty tempfile → `mv` silently truncating `whitelist.local.txt` to zero bytes. Post-fix: fail-closed posture (AC 3 boundary) preserved, fd-201 mutation-lock released on fail path (`exec 201>&-` before `exit 3`) so the next cmd_remove isn't blocked. **Verification:** `bash -n packages/devbox/scripts/whitelist.sh` → PASS; `grep -n '\|\| true' packages/devbox/scripts/whitelist.sh` → remaining hits confined to (a) cmd_sync diff-block `:216,221,222,232,237` (DISMISSED at CR opener — empty-diff/empty-sort/zero-count are valid), (b) `chmod 2>/dev/null || true` at `:242,258` (AI-3 next target). No collateral changes. **LESSON — when replacing `|| true` error-suppression with an rc-capture idiom, pair `|| rc=$?` with `(( rc > N ))` numeric comparison (NOT `[[ $rc -eq N ]]`) if the "tolerated" rc spans a range.** `grep` tolerates rc=1 (all-matched empty output, legitimate); rc=2+ is a family of real errors (2 = read error, 2+ = various I/O/perm faults). `(( rc > 1 ))` correctly accepts rc=0 + rc=1 and rejects rc≥2 as a single range. `[[ $rc -eq 1 ]] || fail` inverted — reads as "rc=1 OK, everything else fails" which rejects rc=0 (match found). The `|| rc=$?` idiom preserves `set -e` compatibility because the `||` consumes grep's non-zero exit before errexit fires. Apply to every future `|| true` → error-surfacing conversion: (1) declare `local rc=0`, (2) capture via `|| rc=$?`, (3) use numeric range comparison `(( rc > N ))` for multi-tolerance bands, (4) release any held locks/fds BEFORE `exit` on the fail branch so resources don't leak. **LESSON — AI-N surgical-Edit drain iters are holding at ~8K tokens per iter for user-facing-CLI class (iter-178 matched by iter-179).** Confirms the pattern forecast at iter-177: 5-PATCH drain fits inside ~40K cumulative budget (5 × 8K), tracking the 6-iter chain-length forecast to iter-182 closure + iter-183 CR re-run. **NEXT (iter-180):** AI-3 remove `2>/dev/null || true` from both `chmod 0644` invocations at `whitelist.sh:242,258` — cmd_sync runs as root pre-Story-2.5 so chmod MUST succeed; suppressing stderr hides MAC / ro-mount / perm-bit faults that leave the composed file at mktemp's 0600 → dnsmasq (non-root worker) cannot read the new policy → active-vs-applied divergence. Replace with bare `chmod 0644 "${COMPOSED_WHITELIST}"` + same for PREVIOUS_COMPOSED; `set -e` surfaces the error with chmod's stderr visible. Aligns with Story 2.3 iter-170 AR-9 "fail loud on I/O boundaries" precedent.

Generalisation holds: for any Epic-2 story where (trace ran WAIVED with STRONG substrate evidence) AND (dev-story landed without partial) AND (scope-isolation audit passes on the pre-iter-174 snapshot), the SM opener ZERO-PATCHes by design; the drift risk lies entirely in the CR gate. The `cp` proposal would lose atomicity (a SIGTERM mid-`cp` leaves a half-written target); `mv` is rename(2) atomic on same FS. - **2026-04-21 (Story 2.3 iter-158): `/bmad-dev-story` Story 2.3 landed in a single iteration — FR14n `atdd-scaffolded → in-dev`; sprint-status `ready-for-dev → review`; story `Status: review`.** Single-iter landing on a ~650 LOC / 11-new-files / 11-modified-files story holds as the second Epic-2 precedent (2.2 iter-148 was 8-task hybrid; 2.3 is 13-task infrastructure-security — larger surface, same single-iter discipline). Budget consumed: ~70K tokens — well under the ≥80K projection. **Sync-gate protocol (Task 10.5) worked cleanly on first roundtrip:** manifest entry for `INV-devbox-egress-contract` registered with placeholder contentHash `0000…0000` → `node packages/keel-invariants/dist/check.js` surfaces `actualHash=aad16a51aa1dc7527c0312e6b99217966d7f3f3478fb677dd347792e9cb6889b` in structured JSON on stdout → paste back → re-run → exit 0 green. Story 2.2 iter-153 established this protocol; iter-158 re-validated on a `docs/invariants/` target. 5-field `InvariantSchema` held (`id`, `description`, `sourcePath`, `contentHash`, `anchors`; no `name` key — iter-156 PATCH 1 carry-forward). Backtick-wrapped stable-ID in `anchors` array + matching `INVARIANTS.md` anchor bullet confirmed (19+1 existing entries all use this shape). **LESSON — non-obvious nftables chain-scope correction applied vs iter-155/156/157 template draft wording.** The v1.1/v1.2 Task 4 spec implied `meta nfproto ipv4` (bare match line at chain top) would scope the chain to IPv4 packets. That's not how nftables works: in an `inet`-family table with two chains hooked at the SAME priority (`output_v4` + `output_v6`, both at `type filter hook output priority 0`), every output packet traverses BOTH chains. A bare `meta nfproto ipv4` match without a verdict is meaningless (and would fail `nft -c -f` parse); and even with a verdict, a "policy drop + conditional accept rules" layout would accidentally double-drop non-target-family packets via each chain's policy drop when they fall through without matching any target-family rule. **The idiomatic pattern is `meta nfproto != <target-family> accept` as the FIRST rule of each chain:** short-circuits non-target-family traffic to `accept` before any other rule evaluates, preserving per-chain family scope, keeping `policy drop` authoritative ONLY for the target family. SC-7 verbatim assertion `nft list chain inet keel_egress output_v4/output_v6 | grep -q 'policy drop'` still passes (policy line is unchanged). Implementation landed in `packages/devbox/nftables/egress.nft`. Apply whenever future stories author multi-chain nftables rulesets in an `inet`-family table at the same priority — NEVER rely on `meta nfproto <family>` as a chain-scope filter; use `meta nfproto != <family> accept` as the first rule. **LESSON — every live-verification Task 12.X on backend-B iteration-env must carry the SC-7/AC-mapped `docker exec` recipe pinned in both the invariant doc § Verification + README § Egress policy § Verification BEFORE dev-story close.** At iter-158 I pinned all 5 AC-mapped recipes (resolv.conf pin, IPv4/IPv6 parity, fail-closed unwhitelisted, JSONL schema round-trip, atomic reload) verbatim in both files — operator can `docker exec keel-devbox <recipe>` without re-deriving. Prior Story 2.1 iter-144 + Story 2.2 iter-148 deferred smokes to operator WITHOUT pinned commands, forcing the operator to re-read SC clauses to reconstruct verification. Story 2.3's commit-time pin closes that gap for this story class; apply at every future infrastructure-class story with backend-B live-smoke defers. **LESSON — `packages/devbox/scripts/*.sh` shape holds exactly as Story 2.1 `benchmark.sh` pinned it.** All four new scripts (`start-egress.sh`, `reload-egress.sh`, `egress-log-tailer.sh`, `monitor.sh`) pass `bash -n` syntax check; `#!/usr/bin/env bash`, `set -euo pipefail`, `0755`, kebab-case + `.sh` discipline identical across all four. Confirms the shape is template-level copy-ready for every future `packages/devbox/scripts/` addition — do not hand-design new shell conventions; clone Story 2.1's `benchmark.sh` header. **LESSON — Change Log per-file convention: Story 2.3 uses NEWEST-FIRST (v1.3 above v1.2 above v1.1 above v1.0).** Story 2.2 used chronological-append-at-tail. Before writing a new Change Log entry, read the last ~5 lines of the target file's Change Log section to detect convention — DO NOT assume. iter-158 prepended v1.3 above v1.2 per the per-file convention established at iter-157 for Story 2.3. Generalizes to every future story-file authored by a different author-cycle that might pick a different convention. **LESSON — nftables `meta nfproto != X accept` short-circuit vs naive `meta nfproto X` match: the spec-author's mental model may not match nftables kernel semantics; verify semantics BEFORE pinning verbatim commands in the spec.** Story 2.3's v1.0 / v1.1 / v1.2 drafts all carried the `meta nfproto ipv4` bare-match phrasing — none of the SM / ATDD / subagent review caught the semantic issue because `grep -q 'policy drop'` on the chain listing is insensitive to the chain body rules. Future infrastructure-class stories with kernel-privileged deliverables (nftables, cgroups, eBPF, seccomp, apparmor) should carry an explicit "validated-against-kernel-semantics" note at SM validation — the current SM review is spec-coherence-only, not kernel-semantics-aware. Proposal for Story 2.4 (whitelist CLI) dev-agent: flag kernel-semantics-dependent SC clauses for ultrathink verification at draft time. **NEXT:** `/bmad-testarch-trace (args: "yolo")` for `in-dev → traced`. - **2026-04-21 (Story 2.2 iter-153): AR-2 drained — `.envrc.local.example` removed from allow-list contract sentence in `docs/invariants/gitignored-secret-commit-deny.md:57` + `INV-gitignored-secret-commit-deny` contentHash refreshed (`54ef4340… → e0c70aa4…`) + sync-gate exit 0 + positive smoke (`packages/devbox/.envrc.example` → exit 0) + negative smoke (`/tmp/.envrc` → exit 1 with pointer) end-to-end green.** Second of the two iter-151 PATCHes; both now drained (iter-152 AR-1 + iter-153 AR-2). Root cause recap: doc claimed `.envrc.local.example` EXEMPT via anchored regex end-match, but `.gitignore` has no `!.envrc.local.example` negation — `.env*` silently ignores it → doc-contract drift from gitignore behaviour (not from script behaviour; the hook regex end-match claim itself is accurate). Conservative fix: remove the filename from the sentence (AC 1 + AC 4 never name it as a committed companion), leave `.gitignore` + regex unchanged. Budget: ~6K tokens (Edit + sha256 + Edit + build + sync-gate + 2 smokes). **LESSON — "doc-contract drift" is the dominant CR-patch class for manifest-tracked invariant docs.** Both iter-151 PATCHes (AR-1 + AR-2) were the same class: the invariant doc made a claim (an example CLI exit code OR an allow-list exemption) that the actual substrate (basename-anchored regex OR `.gitignore` negation rules) did not honour. The manifest's `contentHash` field freezes the doc text at a snapshot but does NOT verify that the text's CLAIMS re-compile against the ACTUAL substrate behaviour — the sync-gate detects textual drift, not semantic drift. Apply at every future invariant-doc author-cycle: when quoting a regex, CLI exit code, or gitignore rule inline, grep the actual substrate and run the actual command at author-time (not just at CR-time). Pattern: `grep <claim> <canonical-substrate-file>` OR `<run-the-cli-invocation>` then `echo $?` → paste the VERIFIED value into the doc. **LESSON — the conservative-fix heuristic for doc-contract drift is "remove the unverifiable claim" not "add substrate to match the claim".** AR-2 could have been fixed two ways: (a) remove `.envrc.local.example` from the doc sentence; (b) add `!.envrc.local.example` to `.gitignore`. Choice (a) is conservative because Story 2.2 AC 1 + AC 4 never committed to allowing that filename — the doc drifted beyond the story's scope. Choice (b) would expand AC scope without a spec mandate + introduce a new committable schema companion that no story consumes. Apply at every future doc-drift CR triage: prefer "narrow the doc" over "widen the substrate" unless the story's AC text explicitly requires the substrate expansion. **LESSON — the forecast-envelope equation from iter-151 v1.5 SM is on track.** iter-151 projected Story 2.2 `done` at iter-154 (AR-1 iter-152 + AR-2 iter-153 + CR re-run iter-154); landed on schedule with zero unplanned iterations. Apply at every future CR entry: trust the forecast when the patch count ≤ 2 and both patches are narrow doc-only fixes; fan-out / adversarial triage budget should go to CR re-run rather than mid-stream re-estimation. **NEXT:** iter-154 `/bmad-code-review (args: "2")` re-run for `fixes-pending → done` confirmation. Expect ZERO-PATCH close (no new findings expected given narrow doc-only churn) OR a 1–2 AI cycle if Blind/Edge/Auditor surface regressions from the doc-correction text. If another cycle surfaces, it would push `done` to iter-155+ — record and forecast-envelope again at that point.

Applies to every future story that adds`.envrc.example`knobs on top of a prior story's existing compose knob surface. **GOTCHA — task spec`/tmp/fake.envrc` as a lint-rule negative smoke case is inconsistent with the AC 5 regex (`/^(.+\/)?\.envrc$/`only matches paths whose basename is literally`.envrc`, `.envrc.local`, or `.secrets`—`fake.envrc`has no leading dot so doesn't match).** Correct negative smoke uses`/tmp/.envrc`. iter-148 Dev Notes record this drift so future CR-re-runs don't re-raise it as a finding. **GOTCHA — `git check-ignore -v`exit-code semantics vary by git version.** Git 2.43 (iteration container) exits 0 with the matching rule printed even when that rule is a`!`-negation (the file is NOT ignored in practice); older git versions emit "exit 1 no output" for negation-matched paths. The story spec's prescribed behaviour follows the older git convention. Functional verification pattern that's git-version-independent: `git check-ignore`(no`-v`) returns exit 1 on un-ignored paths + `git status --short`shows`??`for untracked files +`git add --dry-run`shows`add 'path'`for stageable files. iter-148 used this pattern to confirm the`.envrc.example`+`.secrets.example`schemas are stageable despite the gitignore block; the`-v`output was treated as informational, not authoritative. **GOTCHA —`prek`binary is NOT installed in the Ralph iteration container's PATH** (declared as devDependency at`package.json:27`but`node_modules/.bin/`not populated here). Direct`pnpm exec prek run …`fails with`command not found`. Workaround: node-direct (`node packages/keel-invariants/dist/check-no-committed-dotfiles.js <args>`) + pnpm-script (`pnpm keel-invariants:no-committed-dotfiles <args>`) substitute with identical semantics at the script layer. Full prek integration (hook ordering + `files:`regex scoping + pre-commit pipeline flow) is operator-workstation + CI coverage. Carry-forward: future prek-hook-authoring stories (Epic 4 SAST hooks, Epic 13 CI-harness hooks) can't rely on`pnpm exec prek`inside the iteration container; verify the hook's underlying script directly + defer prek-runner integration to operator / CI. **NEXT:**`/bmad-testarch-trace (args: "yolo")` for AC→test coverage gate; expect WAIVED per Story 2.1 iter-126 + Epic 1 ten-precedent pattern (infrastructure-smoke + configuration-surface hybrid class) — twelfth cumulative.

Budget: iter-146 total token usage ~60K (three parallel Explores ~30K aggregate + 9 targeted Edit calls + IP + RALPH.md); well under the 117K execution budget. **LESSON — resolve "decide at implementation time" ambiguities AT REVIEW TIME via cross-file precedent lookup, not at dev-time.** Story 2.2's Open Question #3 cited AI-7 iter-135 but deferred the choice; iter-146's Review 2 subagent read `invariants.manifest.ts:252` directly + confirmed doc-first precedent; story updated to RESOLVED. Same cost paid once in review vs guessed-wrong in dev (one-iteration sync-gate hash mismatch). **LESSON — `.pre-commit-config.yaml`'s `files:` regex filter is the right scoping mechanism for prek hooks with `pass_filenames: true`.** Matches the existing `tokens-schema` + `tokens-contrast` hooks at `.pre-commit-config.yaml:31,37`. Without `files:`, prek invokes the hook on every staged file at every commit — wasteful even when the hook exits 0 fast for non-matches. Added `files: '(^|/)\\.(envrc|envrc\\.local|secrets)$'` to the Story 2.2 AC5 hook template. Pattern for future prek-hook-authoring stories: scope invocation via `files:` regex, pass filenames via `pass_filenames: true`. **LESSON — AC1↔AC2 internal consistency audit is a Layer-6 preventative review** (adds to the Layers 1-5 established at iter-54 + iter-72 + iter-79): when an AC enumerates a set (knob list, column set, file set, key set), verify the matching downstream AC's mapping table / compose field list / schema / gitignore / default-value block contains EXACTLY that set — no extras, no omissions. iter-146 found `KEEL_DEVBOX_TMPFS_LOGS_MB` shipped in reference-defaults but not in AC1's enumerated knob list; the Layer-6 audit catches that specific drift class. Carry-forward: iter-147+ `/bmad-create-story` + `/bmad-create-story (args: "review")` should add explicit AC1↔AC2↔... cross-AC enumeration-set audit. **GOTCHA — prek `files:` + `pass_filenames: true` interaction.** `files:` controls WHEN prek invokes the hook (only if a staged file matches the regex); `pass_filenames: true` controls WHAT argv prek passes (the matched filenames). Combining both = hook only runs when relevant AND gets the filenames for in-place matching. Wrong combination: `pass_filenames: false` + no `files:` would invoke on every commit with no argv (script would need to re-invoke git — wasteful). Wrong combination: `pass_filenames: true` + no `files:` would invoke on every commit with ALL staged filenames — also wasteful. **NEXT:** `/bmad-testarch-atdd` for Story 2.2 red-phase scaffolds; state `validated → atdd-scaffolded`. Mixed scope (lint-rule TS = Vitest-natural; dotfile schemas + compose + gitignore = infrastructure-smoke): let the atdd skill decide; record FR14n skip rationale in IP if partial-skip ensues.

- **2026-04-21 (Story 2.1 iter-140): CR-re-run fix AR-2 (Medium) landed — `fixes-pending` QUEUE drains 2/5.** `packages/devbox/entrypoint.sh` gains two bundled hardening edits at AI-5's surface: (a) `chown_err="$(mktemp -t chown.XXXXXX)"` at L68 replaces AI-5's hard-coded `/tmp/chown.err`; both chown sites (workspace L80-85 + named-volume loop L91-99) use the per-invocation process-unique path, so Story 2.11 shared-mode + back-to-back `docker compose run --rm` cannot clobber each other's stderr captures or cleanup rms. (b) Regex anchor widens `^[A-Za-z0-9_-]+:[A-Za-z0-9_-]+$` → `^[A-Za-z_][A-Za-z0-9_.+-]*:[A-Za-z_][A-Za-z0-9_.+-]*$`; first-char `[A-Za-z_]` still rejects leading digits + leading `-` (POSIX username shape + AI-5's option-parse-injection defence); tail adds `.` + `+` for enterprise AD/LDAP-mapped names like `first.last:eng` / `dev+ops:team`. Both edits wrapped in AI-5-pattern rationale-comment blocks (11 + 12 lines). Verification: `bash -n` OK; Task 7.1 forbidden-pattern grep still exit 1 (new text doesn't contain `npm install|pip install|curl|wget…|sh` literals — LESSON-59 holds); Task 7.4 `100755` preserved; concurrent-run smoke ran 50 A/B pairs with chown failing to non-existent paths → `collisions=0` + content-isolation PASS; regex accepts 4/4 spec cases + rejects 4/4 + 4 adversarial extras PASS. **LESSON — when the smoke target is `entrypoint.sh` itself but the script body assumes root + `/workspace` + `/home/dev/...` existence under `set -e`, a stand-in script that extracts the specific mechanics (mktemp + tmpfile-capture + fail-target chown) is the right verification tool.** iter-139 established the same pattern for benchmark.sh (stand-in replacing `docker compose down` with a no-op for trap-semantics validation). Applies to every future entrypoint.sh / benchmark.sh hardening iteration where the full script can't run cleanly under the iteration container's non-root / missing-path / missing-daemon constraints. **LESSON — bundling AR findings that cluster on the same AI-landed-surface is strictly better than two sequential iterations.** AR-2 (a) + AR-2 (b) both live inside AI-5's iter-133 commit region (regex-validation + capture-chown-stderr). A single edit + single rationale-comment-pair + single commit preserves one-task-per-iteration discipline because the "task" is the bundle surface, not the individual line edits. iter-132's four-edit AI-4 bundle is the canonical precedent (SIGINT trap + docker info probe + flag-combo warning + native-A vs DinD flag text all shipped in one iteration). iter-139 AR-1 bundled three trap-infrastructure edits (INT/TERM split + HUP/QUIT coverage + ERR via EXIT). Future CR-re-run iterations: when two or more findings share a file + share a rationale surface, bundle. **GOTCHA — `mktemp -t chown.XXXXXX` is the deprecated GNU form but still works on Debian Bookworm + Ubuntu 24.04 LTS (the container OS).** Modern `mktemp --tmpdir chown.XXXXXX` or `mktemp "${TMPDIR:-/tmp}/chown.XXXXXX"` are also acceptable; the spec explicitly said `mktemp -t chown.XXXXXX` so I kept that literal form. If a future Ralph lands a `mktemp` call on a non-GNU (e.g. Alpine / BusyBox) base, the `-t` form may behave differently — switch to the `--tmpdir` form or the explicit `${TMPDIR:-/tmp}/prefix.XXXXXX` form. **GOTCHA — POSIX 3.437 portable username character set includes `.` but NOT `+`; the widened regex intentionally goes beyond portable** to accept AD/LDAP-mapped names that actual enterprise operators use. `chown` passes the string through to the underlying syscall; if the name doesn't resolve, chown returns an error which AI-5's capture-and-re-emit path surfaces. The widening is a usability choice, not a correctness weakening — the option-parse-injection defence (via `[A-Za-z_]` anchor on first char + `chown --` belt-and-braces) is preserved unconditionally. **NEXT:** AR-3 (Low) — `packages/devbox/VERSIONS.md` doc-drift bundle: (a) Supabase CLI row "Arch-aware fallback; skipped if asset missing for host." → "Fail-closed if asset missing for host arch (matches git-delta pattern per iter-134 AI-6)"; (b) uv (Astral) row `_recorded-at-bake_` → `0.11.7 (iter-123 bake capture)` matching AI-1 claude-code precedent. Then AR-4 → AR-5 → third CR re-run → `fixes-pending → done`.

- **2026-04-21 (Story 2.1 iter-139): CR-re-run fix AR-1 (Medium) landed — `fixes-pending` QUEUE drains 1/5.** `packages/devbox/scripts/benchmark.sh` — AI-4's unified `trap 'compose down; exit 130' INT TERM` replaced with centralised EXIT-trap cleanup + per-signal `exit N` wrappers (INT=130, TERM=143, HUP=129, QUIT=131 per POSIX 128+signum). Three defects collapsed into one infrastructure edit: (a) INT/TERM shared 130 under AI-4 conflated the two signals for any `$?`-reading supervisor; (b) HUP + QUIT uncovered → closed terminal / Ctrl-\\ leaked compose stack; (c) ERR path uncovered → `set -e` on failed `docker compose build`/`up` (the iter-124 bind-mount-denial abort class) leaked half-created image + container + network. Centralising cleanup in EXIT trap (fires on ANY exit — signal / ERR / normal) subsumes all three. Per-signal `exit N` → EXIT handoff is safe because bash doesn't re-enter EXIT during its own execution — `cleanup_on_exit` fires exactly once with signal-specific `$?` and `exit "$exit_code"` at the tail belt-and-braces the status propagation. Verification: `bash -n` OK; stand-in smoke (docker-compose-down replaced with no-op for Docker-less iteration shell) validated all six paths — normal rc=0; `false` under `set -e` rc=1 (AR-1 (c) target: ERR now covered); INT rc=130; TERM rc=143 (previously 130); HUP rc=129 + QUIT rc=131 (previously uncovered). **LESSON — trap centralisation via EXIT wrapper is the right refactor when multiple signal-trap CR findings cluster around the same cleanup primitive.** Per-signal traps reduce to one-line `exit N` wrappers; the `set -e` ERR path falls out for free (EXIT fires regardless of exit origin); future signals (USR1/USR2 if ever needed) are one-liners. AI-4's original unified `INT TERM` trap was correct for its single-defect scope (iter-124 bind-mount-denial ^C); the iter-138 CR's F1+F27+F28 cluster revealed the abstraction was one layer too shallow. Applies to every future script that wants "cleanup on exit" semantics: prefer EXIT trap + thin per-signal exit wrappers over `trap 'CLEANUP; exit N' SIG1 SIG2 …`. **LESSON — stand-in smoke scripts are the right verification tool for Docker-less iteration contexts when the edit under test is wiring, not Docker semantics.** The AR-1 edit changes trap infrastructure, not `docker compose down` behaviour; replacing `docker compose down` with `: >/dev/null 2>&1 || true` in a stand-in test isolates what actually changed and validates it without needing a live daemon / bind-mount-compatible workspace. The operator-workstation run inherits the wiring transparently. Applies whenever future CR fix-passes touch trap / signal / set -e infrastructure under the backend-B bind-mount-denial carve-out. **GOTCHA — bash EXIT trap `$?` capture must happen BEFORE any other command runs inside the trap body.** `local exit_code=$?; docker compose down …; exit "$exit_code"` captures the triggering status first; writing `docker compose down …; local exit_code=$?; exit "$exit_code"` would capture the `down` command's status instead (it's idempotent but can still exit non-zero if the daemon has gone away). Both forms have shipped in the wild in other projects — ours uses the former deliberately. **NEXT:** AR-2 (entrypoint.sh concurrency + charset hardening: `mktemp`-based chown.err capture + widened `KEEL_DEVBOX_WORKSPACE_OWNER` regex for POSIX-valid enterprise usernames with `.` or `+`). Then AR-3 → AR-4 → AR-5 → third CR re-run → `fixes-pending → done`.

- **2026-04-21 (Story 2.1 iter-124): Backend-B iteration-context bind-mount denial — extends operator-owned carve-out from cold-prune to ALL bind-mount-based compose runtime.** Empirical outcome of the iter-123-decomposed exercise half: Task 7.3 (`docker compose -f packages/devbox/docker-compose.yml config`) exits 0 with a cleanly resolved YAML — ✓ in-iteration. Task 4 (`docker compose run --rm devbox pnpm test`) + Task 5-run (`scripts/benchmark.sh --skip-cold` → `docker compose up -d`) both fail with `Error response from daemon: mounts denied: <worktree> is not shared from the host and is not known to Docker`. Root cause: under backend B (host socket-passthrough from iteration container), the compose bind-mount source (`${KEEL_DEVBOX_WORKSPACE:-../..}` resolving to the worktree root `/workspace/ralph-bmad/.claude/worktrees/<name>`) is an iteration-container-internal path invisible to the host Docker Desktop daemon's File Sharing allowlist (which defaults to `/Users`, `/tmp`, `/private`, `/Volumes`). Confirmed by targeted probes: `docker run --rm -v /tmp:/mnt alpine ls /mnt` → ✓ (lists host `/private/tmp` content, e.g. `com.apple.launchd.*`); `docker run --rm -v "$PWD":/mnt alpine ls /mnt` → same `mounts denied` error. **LESSON — backend-B iteration-context operational constraint:** `docker compose build` works (build context is streamed as a tarball to the daemon, no bind mounts at build time); ANY subsequent `docker compose run` / `up -d` / `compose exec` against a compose file with workspace bind mounts fails unless the source path happens to coincide with a host-shared path. **GOTCHA — `benchmark.sh` warm-only pass under backend B from iteration context is not workable; the iter-122 `detect_backend()` + cold-prune refusal gate is necessary but INSUFFICIENT.** `--skip-cold` skips the destructive prune but the subsequent `compose up -d` still hits the mount denial. The script fails cleanly via `set -euo pipefail` (no malformed README entry written, good), but a future iteration could add a pre-flight bind-mount probe (`docker run --rm -v "${workspace}":/_probe alpine:latest true`) to fail earlier with operator-guidance text. **Deferred to QUEUE** — keeping iter-124 scope tight. **LESSON — IP's hypothesis was partially wrong.** IP framed Task 4 outcome as "no test runner configured at root → non-zero exit per Epic-1-through-13 precedent". The actual outcome is "container creation refused by daemon before pnpm ever executes". These are different failure modes; the iter-1..iter-13 no-test-runner precedent doesn't apply here. The lesson: when predicting a dynamic-runtime outcome, account for every gate between invocation and target-process execution (CLI dispatch → compose resolution → bind-mount validation → image pull → container create → entrypoint exec → command invocation). Failure at an earlier gate replaces the hypothesised outcome. **OPERATIONAL IMPLICATION:** Story 2.1 Tasks 4 + 5-run join the operator-owned AC-4 cold-NFR2 carve-out. Story State stays `in-dev (partial)` until an operator run closes them. iter-125 re-invokes `/bmad-dev-story` with this empirical delta in hand: Task 7.3 → closed in-iteration; Tasks 4 + 5-run → scope re-documented as operator-owned (like cold NFR2), story text updated, Story State advances `in-dev (partial) → in-dev`, then queue `/bmad-testarch-trace (args: "yolo")`. This is a bounded scope extension of the iter-122 backend-B carve-out, not a new blocker.

- **2026-04-21 (Story 2.1 iter-123): First successful devbox image bake (safe-subset, backend B).** Closes the iter-100..120 detection-gated wait pattern. `docker compose -f packages/devbox/docker-compose.yml build` produced `keel-devbox:local` (image ID `e7e91f1537f1`, 848 MB, `linux/arm64`) in ~4.5 min aggregate stage time; all toolchain versions captured from inside the baked image (node 20.20.2, pnpm 10.29.2, @anthropic-ai/claude-code 2.1.116, gh 2.90.0, uv 0.11.7, AWS CLI v2 2.34.33, Supabase CLI 2.90.0, git-delta 0.19.2, psql 16.13, Ubuntu 24.04.4 LTS); VERSIONS.md § Bake log updated with the full matrix + build stats. Backend-B safety contract held — additive `compose build` + `compose run --rm` only, no `docker system prune`. Next iter (124) exercises the baked image via `compose run --rm devbox pnpm test` + `pnpm lint` + `benchmark.sh --skip-cold`, then iter-125 re-invokes `/bmad-dev-story` to formally close Tasks 4 + 5-run + 7.3 and flip Story State `in-dev (partial) → in-dev`. **GOTCHA — `docker compose build … | tee log.log` masks non-zero exit codes.** First bake attempt this iter hit a transient `dial tcp 127.0.0.1:443: connect: connection refused` on `auth.docker.io` (buildkit metadata fetch for `ubuntu:24.04`), but the completion notification reported `exit code 0` because `tee` always exits 0 — the pipeline's exit is tee's, not docker's. **LESSON — when exit status matters, redirect with `> log 2>&1` not `| tee log`; OR `set -o pipefail` + check `PIPESTATUS[0]`.** Applies to any long-running build / script a Ralph iteration tees for visibility. **GOTCHA — `cmd > log 2>&1 &` inside a Bash tool invocation backgrounds the wrapper shell further, and the "background command completed exit 0" notification fires when the WRAPPER exits instantly, NOT when the build finishes.** Second attempt this iter hit the same trap. Mitigation: don't nest `&` inside a `run_in_background: true` Bash call (the harness already backgrounds); OR attach a `Monitor` task to `tail -f` the log with a terminal-state grep alternation (`DONE|ERROR|failed to solve|naming to`) and treat the Monitor events as ground truth for completion. iter-123 used the second path — Monitor events tracked `#3` through `#21 naming to …` as the real completion signal. **GOTCHA — transient buildkit `127.0.0.1:443` on `auth.docker.io` recovered after direct `docker pull ubuntu:24.04` succeeded.** Root cause not fully nailed (likely transient buildx builder state or a Docker Desktop credential-helper quirk on the operator host); mitigation pattern held: direct pull the base → retry `compose build` → success. Add a "pre-pull FROM targets" step to the bake playbook if this recurs. **LESSON — IP § Notes guardrail-9 decomposition call WAS correct.** NOW at iter-123 entry wrapped bake + test/lint + benchmark + version capture + VERSIONS append as one atomic outcome; decomposing into iter-123 = bake+versions+VERSIONS and iter-124 = test/lint+benchmark kept the execution ceiling inside a single ~117K budget cleanly. Future Epic 2 Docker-gated stories should copy this split pattern.

- **2026-04-21 (Story 2.1 iter-122): DinD backend is `B` (host socket-passthrough), NOT `A` (isolated DinD) — critical safety correction to iter-121.** Empirical discovery on entry: `docker info --format '{{.Name}}'` → `docker-desktop`; `docker ps -a` lists host-level containers from the operator's unrelated "web-signals" supabase project, `sec-edgar-mcp`, and the cc-devbox container I'm running in. `/var/run/docker.sock` is bind-mounted from the macOS host (Mar 30 datestamp, predates this cc-devbox rebuild). **`docker run --rm hello-world` exits 0** — the functional criterion holds; iter-121's reachability claim was correct, but the BACKEND assumption (isolated DinD) was wrong. **Safety implication: `benchmark.sh`'s `docker system prune -af --volumes` cold-pass would DESTROY all host-level unrelated-project state.** Added backend-B safety guard to `packages/devbox/scripts/benchmark.sh`: `detect_backend()` matches `docker-desktop`/`moby`/`linuxkit-*` or uses `/.dockerenv` + hostname heuristic; refuses destructive cold-pass under backend B unless `--allow-broad-prune` override is set; `--skip-cold` runs warm-only (safe under either backend). Rewrote `docs/invariants/devbox-dind.md` with § Backend contract + § Safety rule (A = isolated, broad prune self-contained; B = socket-passthrough, broad prune escapes container); added `docker run hello-world` to the functional criterion; updated `INV-devbox-dind-available` manifest description + contentHash (`81af7752…0c32` was wrong — on-disk was `e57f77e4…4227`; after this iter's rewrite the authoritative hash is `a9675f7d…b3ad`). Added AGENTS.md § Devbox iteration environment paragraph on backends + safety rule. **LESSON — always verify "DinD" claims empirically.** `docker info` + `docker ps -a` on entry distinguishes backend A from B in ~2 tool calls. An iter-121-style "operator installed Docker, we're good" signpost can hide a socket-passthrough arrangement whose safety semantics are MATERIALLY different from isolated DinD — and a script written for A can be catastrophic under B. At every "DinD" claim in a signpost / invariant / story, add a backend-detect line. **LESSON — speculative doc drafts that reference unverified empirical claims pollute the invariant surface.** The iter-121-authored `docs/invariants/devbox-dind.md` included a fabricated "iter-122 discovered unshare: operation not permitted at layer registration" block — iter-122 (this iter) did NOT discover that; `hello-world` exits 0 cleanly. Some prior writer (an agent run that was never committed, or a plan-mode iter) pre-emptively drafted a speculative failure narrative. Rule: invariant docs MUST cite empirical evidence contemporaneous with the doc's commit; speculative failure narratives are for RALPH.md signposts or BLOCKED entries, not for `docs/invariants/`. **LESSON — iter-121 manifest contentHash drift: `81af7752…0c32` in the manifest did NOT match on-disk `e57f77e4…4227`.** iter-121 either hashed a draft then modified the file, or copy-pasted the hash from a prior source. Story 1.9's sync-gate would catch this at pre-merge; at 1.0 it's spec-enforced only, so the drift rode in. Mitigation: at every manifest entry authoring, IMMEDIATELY re-hash via `sha256sum <sourcePath>` as a final step and compare to the manifest entry. **LESSON — iter-121 was partial: documentation + manifest entry were written but never committed.** The uncommitted diff at iter-122 entry (`AGENTS.md`, `INVARIANTS.md`, `RALPH.md`, `architecture.md`, `manifest.ts` modified; `devbox-dind.md` untracked) represents iter-121's full intended delivery. iter-122 bundled the correction + safety guard with iter-121's staged work in one commit (step 3a permits IP + knowledge-file changes to commit alongside source work). **Next iter-123:** now that benchmark.sh is backend-safe, the safe-subset operator-bake (`docker compose build` additive + `docker compose run --rm devbox pnpm test/lint` additive + version capture) runs in-iteration without risk to host state. Cold NFR2 measurement remains an explicit M4-Pro native task (queued as operator-owned external signal, not Ralph-owned in-iteration). iter-124+ re-invokes `/bmad-dev-story` to close Tasks 4 + 5-run + 7.3 and advance Story State `in-dev (partial) → in-dev`.

When state is inconsistent (sprint-status drift, missing next-epic row, PR query fails, IP § Context conflicts with sprint-status), Ralph falls back to `EPIC_DONE` with a diagnostic `note` field — not a new waiting reason. All 6 quality gates green first pass (typecheck / lint / build / format:check / prek / sync-gate). **Determinism smoke 1 (byte-identical round-trip): PASS** — 5 consecutive identical-hash runs across smoke 1 + smoke 2 edit/revert + final verify. **Determinism smoke 2 (source-change propagation + revert-to-baseline): PASS** — edit accent.500 54%→55% → all 3 outputs change + alias-downstream propagation verified (`accent.default`, `text.accent`, `state.in-progress` all pick up new value via multi-hop DFS flattening) → revert → byte-identical with baseline. **NEW LESSON — emitter-owned-byte-format decision (generated-file prettier ignore).** When the emitter's native output diverges from prettier's reformatting (OKLCH decimal normalization `0.20 → 0.2`; CSS attribute-selector quote conversion `[data-theme="dark"] → [data-theme='dark']`; TS double-quote → single-quote), the simpler determinism-preserving path is adding the generated files to `.prettierignore` and declaring the emitter's byte output as canonical. Alternative (embed prettier API inside the emitter) adds a runtime dep + async main + prettier-version coupling. Pattern: prettier owns the emitter SOURCE file (which it fully governs); emitter owns the GENERATED outputs (byte-stability is the emit contract, not a prettier contract). Apply at Story 1.13+ gate-emitter + Story 5+ `@keel/keel-generator` output formats + any future emit-target pair. **NEW LESSON — story-text literal command vs command intent.** Story § AC 1 carve-out proposed `git rev-parse --short=12 HEAD -- <path>` literally for source-SHA resolution, but `rev-parse` returns repo HEAD (the `--` is a rev/path separator, not a log filter). The correct command matching the carve-out's stated INTENT ("file's latest commit, NOT HEAD of the repo") is `git log -1 --format=%h --abbrev=12 -- <path>`. Emitter uses the intent-matching command; documented in the emitter source-file header block + Debug Log. Pattern for future stories: when a story-pinned command contradicts the surrounding prose constraints, prefer intent over the literal command + document the deviation. **Sizing actuals vs iter-60 projection.** iter-60 projected "budget-intensive iteration; multi-pass plausible with `in-dev (partial)` re-queue" — CONFIRMED as single-pass (~55-65K): substrate-tooling story with 3 output stages + manifest reg + 2 smokes + quality gates all fit single iteration. iter-60 Story 1.11 iter-56 precedent held; future emitter-style stories (Story 1.13 gate authoring, Story 5+ generator outputs) are single-pass-candidates when preventative-audit discipline pre-resolves emitter shape ambiguities at drafting time. **Hypothesis (iter-60) REFUTED:** emitter-story CR trajectory may ≠ populator-story trajectory (iter-60 predicted 1-2 PATCH rounds median due to emit-logic complexity); actual dev-story pass was clean on first attempt — the seven preventative-audit layers pre-applied at iter-60 drafting absorbed the emit-logic divergence surfaces (output naming × 3, mode-overlay strategy, digit-segment handling, provenance header format, alias-resolution strategy) before dev time. This iter-56 extends it: `git checkout -- <tracked-file-with-uncommitted-edits>` WIPES the uncommitted edits (the file is restored to HEAD, which predates the story's additions). For Story 1.11 drift-smoke 2 (anchor-removal), `git checkout -- INVARIANTS.md` wiped my Story 1.11 anchor block addition — recovery required re-applying the Edit. **Canonical revert patterns for drift-smoke 2 when the anchor edit is uncommitted:** (a) `cp INVARIANTS.md /tmp/.bak` pre-drift + `cp /tmp/.bak INVARIANTS.md` post-smoke (story 1.10 Task 4 subtask suggestion); (b) re-apply via Edit tool (what I did — works but requires preserving the exact original text); (c) commit the anchor addition BEFORE running drift-smoke 2 then `git checkout --` safely reverts because the anchor is in HEAD (but this breaks the atomic-commit-at-end pattern and creates a commit boundary mid-story). Preferred pattern for Story 1.12+ populator stories: use pattern (a) — tmp-file backup + restore. Cost: 2 extra `cp` invocations. Payoff: no uncommitted-edit wipes. **Sizing actuals vs iter-55 projection.** iter-55 projected `iter-56 in-dev (single-pass)` — confirmed: single-pass, zero partial-completion, all 4 Tasks + 2 smokes + quality gates + sprint-status bump + story-file closure fit in one iteration. Use `git switch -c <new-branch> --no-track origin/main` OR follow immediately with `git branch --unset-upstream` (post-hoc unset works; I used this). If the accidental tracking is left in place and a subsequent `git pull` runs, it pulls `origin/main` into the feature branch — messy but recoverable. **Main checkout blocked in worktree:** `git checkout main` from inside a worktree fails with `fatal: 'main' is already used by worktree at '/workspace/ralph-bmad'` because the main repo owns the main branch. Don't try to check it out locally in the worktree — branch directly from `origin/main` via `git switch -c ... origin/main`. - 2026-04-19: **Story 1.5 Task 2 shipped — both ATDD probes green via real `git commit`, tree restored to Task-1 tip, no Task-1 loop-back.** AC 2 probe: staged `_bmad-output/__ac2-probe.txt` (path under `.prettierignore`, not a TS/lint input — same probe-path strategy Story 1.4 Task 2 settled on after the AC 5 RALPH.md-append landmine), `git commit -m 'fix: resolve edge case in token emitter'` exited 0, all 3 pre-commit hooks Passed, commit-msg `commitlint` Passed, commit landed as `5b05107`, then `git reset --hard HEAD~1` restored to `0092d2b` and removed the probe file in one step. AC 3 probe: `_bmad-output/__ac3-probe.txt`, `git commit -m 'Fixed stuff'`, all 3 pre-commit hooks Passed (message quality is independent of source state — confirms separation of concerns between stages), commit-msg `commitlint` Failed exit 1 with `subject may not be empty [subject-empty]` + `type may not be empty [type-empty]`, commit didn't land (`git log -1` still pointed at `0092d2b` — authoritative AC 3 success signal). Cleanup: `git reset HEAD <file>` + `rm -f <file>` (different recovery from AC 2 because the commit didn't land, so `--hard HEAD~1` isn't applicable). AC 4 structural-only note: git's hook dispatch has zero conditionals on committer identity / `user.name` / environment — Ralph's commits and human commits hit the same `.git/hooks/commit-msg` shim → same prek runner → same commitlint config → same exit criteria; devbox-vs-host parity is structurally implied (Epic 2 scope to verify in-vivo). Quality gates after probe cleanup: typecheck 16/16 FULL TURBO 147ms FIRST call; lint 16/16 FULL TURBO 134ms FIRST call; format:check exit 0; commitlint `--from origin/main --to HEAD --verbose` 0/0 across 3 branch commits (spec + iter-1 + Task 1). **Three carry-forward observations for future ATDD-via-real-`git-commit` work:** (1) **Pre-commit hook output appears DOUBLED through `tee` to a non-tty pipe.** Every hook's name+padding line prints once at start (no result), then prek overwrites in-place via ANSI `\r` with the result line. Tty collapses to one line; pipe captures both. Commitlint's <100ms execution is fast enough to skip the start line — only `Passed`/`Failed` shows. Cosmetic only; not a duplicate-execution bug. The `.pre-commit-config.yaml` has exactly 4 hook entries (3 pre-commit + 1 commit-msg) — verified to rule out config dupes. (2) **`git commit … 2>&1 | tee /tmp/file; echo "$?"` reports `tee`'s exit, NOT git's.** AC 3 probe printed `EXIT=0` from `tee` even though git aborted the commit. The authoritative AC 3 signal is the unchanged branch tip post-probe — proof-by-state, not proof-by-exit-code. For machine-readable git exit via a pipe, use `${PIPESTATUS[0]}` (bash) or split: `git commit … >/tmp/file 2>&1; echo "$?"`. Future ATDD probes that depend on exit-code assertions: avoid the `| tee` pattern unless `PIPESTATUS` is captured. (3) **Two-cleanup-pattern discipline for ATDD probes.** AC-2-style "valid commit lands": `git reset --hard HEAD~1` removes commit + file in one step. AC-3-style "invalid commit rejects": commit didn't land, but staged file remains → `git reset HEAD <file>` + `rm -f <file>`. Pick the right pattern based on whether the probe expected commit success or failure. **Carry-forward landmine for Task 3 verification iteration:** all gates already green at end of Task 2 (FULL TURBO + format:check + commitlint history). Task 3 is sprint-status bump + sprint-status-vs-story-file Status sync + verification-only quality gates; expect FULL TURBO on FIRST gate invocation per Stories 1.2/1.3/1.4 precedent (verification iterations don't touch turbo inputs). **Carry-forward observation:** `pnpm exec prek run --all-files` in Task 3 will run only the 3 pre-commit hooks (commit-msg stage isn't covered by `--all-files`). Commit-msg parity was already proven in Task 1's self-verification probe (via `prek run --stage commit-msg --commit-msg-filename`) and Task 2's AC 2/3 probes (via real `git commit`); no additional commit-msg probe needed in Task 3. Next iteration: Task 3.
