- 2026-04-21: **Entrypoint `exec "$@"` with zero args is a bash no-op — the container exits cleanly with no keepalive (Story 2.1 CR AI-5).** `bash` interprets `exec` with zero args as "apply any I/O redirections to the current shell and return"; the script then proceeds to its end and `set -e` lets the container exit 0. Observed risk: `docker run keel-devbox:local` with no CMD (operator probing the image outside compose) would have quit immediately. Compose's CMD (`sleep infinity`) is the primary path, but relying on the caller to always pass one is a trap. **Rule:** every container entrypoint that ends in `exec "$@"` must guard the empty-args case — `if [ "$#" -eq 0 ]; then exec sleep infinity; else exec "$@"; fi` (or choose a more appropriate keepalive for the service). Also: env-settable identifier fields consumed by system tools (`chown owner`, `chmod mode`, `useradd ...`) should validate their shape with an anchored regex AND pass `--` to terminate option parsing — belt-and-braces defence against `--reference=/etc/shadow` class injection via `.envrc`. Applies to every future entrypoint evolution (Stories 2.3/2.4/2.5/2.8/2.9/2.13).
- 2026-04-21: **Arch-gated Dockerfile RUN blocks that satisfy an unconditional AC must fail-closed, not silent-skip (Story 2.1 CR AI-6).** Pre-fix supabase-cli block's `else` branch at `packages/devbox/Dockerfile:170-172` emitted a "skipping" warning and let the RUN exit 0 when no matching `.deb` asset was found for the target architecture. AC 2 enumerates `supabase-cli` unconditionally — an image built on an exotic arch (linux/arm/v7, linux/riscv64) would ship without the binary and the bake would silently-succeed, producing an artefact that advertises tooling it doesn't have. Mirror pattern is the git-delta block immediately below (L186-193) which already exits 1 on the same failure mode. **Rule:** when a Dockerfile RUN block is gated on `dpkg --print-architecture` and the tool it installs is named in an unconditional AC, the `else` branch is `echo "…: no matching release asset for arch=$arch" >&2; exit 1;` — never a silent-skip. Applies to every future arch-aware install block (Stories 2.3 whitelist/nftables binaries, 2.4 dnsmasq, 2.13 healthcheck tools, 6.1 pg-init utilities, Epic 13 CI harness smokes that bake the image against linux/amd64 in addition to iter-123's linux/arm64). The PATTERN — "if an AC says it must be there, then failing to install it must fail the bake" — is the general rule; the `.deb`-URL-missing branch is just one instantiation.
- 2026-04-21: **Dockerfile shell-form `RUN A && B || C` lets `C` mask a failure of `A` (Story 2.1 CR AI-1).** Pre-fix line at `packages/devbox/Dockerfile:104-105` read `RUN npm install -g @anthropic-ai/claude-code \ && claude --version || true` — the intent was "run install; warn if probe flakes" but shell precedence treats the whole `&& …` chain as the left-hand of `||`, so a failed `npm install` silently resolves to exit 0 via `|| true` and the image bakes with no `claude` binary. **Rule:** in Dockerfile shell-form RUNs, scope `||` to the single command that can legitimately fail by parenthesising: `RUN A && (B || C)` (or use exec-form `RUN ["sh","-c","A && (B || C)"]`). Applies to every future Dockerfile `RUN` that couples a network-install with a post-install probe — Stories 2.3 (whitelist/nftables/dnsmasq), 2.4 (dnsmasq), 2.5 (non-root user), 2.13 (healthcheck), 6.1 (pg-init). Preferred idiom per Story 2.1 CR AI-1 fix: `RUN <install> && (<probe> || echo "<probe> failed (install succeeded)" >&2)` — the stderr diagnostic beats `|| true` because it surfaces probe flakiness without hiding install failures.
- 2026-04-21: **Manifest-build staleness — `pnpm keel-invariants:check` reads `dist/check.js`, not `src/`.** Observed at Story 1.14 iter-77 Task-7 smoke-5: after appending 3 entries to `packages/keel-invariants/src/invariants.manifest.ts`, the manifest-load smoke (`node -e "import('@keel/keel-invariants').then(m => console.log(m.invariants.length))"`) returned `17` pre-rebuild and `20` post-`pnpm --filter @keel/keel-invariants build`. Root cause: `packages/keel-invariants/package.json` points `"exports"` + `"bin"` at compiled `dist/*.js` (tsc emits into `dist/`); the `check` / `check-all` scripts run `node dist/check.js` which imports the compiled, not-yet-updated manifest. Sync-gate silently-passes on stale bytes during the window between source-edit and rebuild → risk of merging a manifest that drifts from the sync-gate's view until someone else rebuilds. **Workaround / rule:** any Ralph iteration that edits `invariants.manifest.ts` (add/modify/remove entry OR update contentHash OR touch Zod schema) MUST run `pnpm --filter @keel/keel-invariants build` BEFORE `pnpm keel-invariants:check` / `check-all` / manifest-load smoke. Quality-gate suite implicitly handles this for future-Ralph: `pnpm typecheck` rebuilds via Turbo cache-miss on source change (dist emit is a side-effect of `tsc -b`), so the standard dev-story sequence (edit manifest → `pnpm typecheck` → `pnpm keel-invariants:check`) works correctly. The failure mode is only visible when running smokes in isolation out-of-order. **Future-Ralph guardrail:** if Task-N smoke returns an unexpected entry count after editing `invariants.manifest.ts`, FIRST check `ls -la packages/keel-invariants/dist/` timestamps vs `src/` timestamps — if src is newer than dist, rebuild. Defer to Story 1.16 whether this is worth automating via a pre-script hook or a dedicated `keel-invariants:check-fresh` script that rebuilds first.
- 2026-04-21: **Unquoted `$(cmd)` or `$(cmd | sort)` as the iterable of a `for` loop word-splits on `IFS` (default `$' \t\n'`) — fragment filenames containing whitespace get torn apart (Story 2.3 CR AR-9).** Original form at `packages/devbox/scripts/start-egress.sh:76` was `for fragment in $(printf '%s\n' "${WHITELIST_FRAGMENTS_DIR}"/*.txt | LC_ALL=C sort); do`: a filename like `team A.txt` expanded into two tokens `team` + `A.txt` — both failed the `[[ -r ]]` guard silently, so that fragment's domains were missing from the composed whitelist with no diagnostic (soft-corruption, not an error). Quoting the substitution (`for x in "$(...)"`) does NOT fix it either — that collapses everything into ONE token. **Rule:** enumerate file-lists via `mapfile -t arr < <(find … -print | sort)` then iterate `for x in "${arr[@]}"`. `mapfile -t` splits on newlines only (safe for whitespace-in-names; still unsafe for newlines-in-names, use `-print0` + `mapfile -d ''` if that's in scope). Prefer `find … -maxdepth 1 -type f -name '*.txt'` over shell glob + `shopt -s nullglob` — `find` gives explicit scoping (no-recursion, files-only) in one line and avoids the nullglob pair. Under bash 4.4+ `set -u`, iterating an empty `mapfile` array is safe (no unbound-var trap). Applies to every future devbox shell-script that lists files by pattern (Stories 2.4 whitelist.sh CLI, 2.5 entrypoint fragments, Epic 13 CI harness fragment fixtures). Verified via 7-probe isolated harness at iter-170 under bash 5.2.21.
- 2026-04-21: **Bash `${array[@]/pattern}` with no replacement blanks the matched element to empty string — it does NOT remove it from the array (Story 2.3 CR AR-8).** `cleanup_files=("${cleanup_files[@]/${dnsmasq_rendered}}")` leaves the array length unchanged with `''` at the matched index; subsequent `for f in "${cleanup_files[@]:-}"` iterations then see the empty entry and only skip it if the consumer carries a `[[ -n "${f}" ]]` guard. Harmless only when every consumer guards empty; intent-obscuring always. **Rule:** to actually remove an element from a bash array, explicit-loop rebuild into a new array and reassign — `new=(); for f in "${arr[@]}"; do [[ "$f" != "$target" ]] && new+=("$f"); done; arr=("${new[@]}")`. Under bash 5.2 + `set -u`, assigning an empty rebuild is safe; if the script must support ancient bash (<4.4), guard with `((${#new[@]})) && arr=("${new[@]}") || arr=()`. Applies to every future devbox shell-script edit (Stories 2.3/2.4/2.5 reload/whitelist/entrypoint evolutions) and to any Epic-13 CI-harness shell helpers. Docs: `bash(1)` § "Parameter Expansion" — `${parameter/pattern/string}` with empty `string` substitutes the empty string, it does not delete.
- 2026-04-20: **`.ralph/halt` is gitignored AND intentionally cleared at startup by `halt.unlink()` in `ralph.py`'s `build_config()`.** Observed historically as "halt doesn't survive ralph.py restarts" — that's the startup-clear at work, not a mystery. Combined with the 2026-04-20 `chore/ralph-halt-path-resolution` fix that resolves halt against the worktree via `$RALPH_BASE_DIR`, the intended flow is: iter N writes halt → ralph.py detects + displays + exits cleanly → user re-runs ralph.py → startup clears halt (so a stale halt can't auto-halt iter 1 of the next session) → iter 1 proceeds. **Pre-fix cascade recipe retired:** the "idempotent halt re-write on re-entry" recipe logged here in iter-22 of Story 1.7 was a workaround for the cwd-mismatch bug, not a genuine ralph.py behaviour. If you see a post-halt re-entry in a post-fix session, check the startup banner (`Ralph base: <abs> (cwd: <abs>)` — first line of every session log) for a resolver mismatch, don't re-write halt blindly.

## Decisions

Choices made with rationale. Useful when a future Ralph wonders "why did past-Ralph do it this way?"

- 2026-04-20: **Scoped `types: ["node"]` to `packages/keel-invariants/tsconfig.json`, NOT `tsconfig.base.json`.** The shared `tsconfig.base.json` is `INV-tsconfig-base`'s `sourcePath` — consumed by every workspace package via `extends`. Adding `types: ["node"]` there would (a) change the substrate hash forcing manifest update, (b) pollute every other package's type roots (including `@keel/ui`, `@keel/contracts`, etc. which don't need Node types), and (c) violate the single-responsibility principle of the shared base config. Scoping to the package's own `tsconfig.json` keeps Node types limited to `@keel/keel-invariants` (where `manifest-reader.ts` / `sync-gate.ts` / `check.ts` live) without affecting any other package. **Carry-forward rule:** Node types (or any other package-specific compiler option) go in the package's local `tsconfig.json`, never in `tsconfig.base.json`. `tsconfig.base.json` stays workspace-wide minimal. Confirmed by Story 1.9 iter-4; will bind Stories 1.10+ adding design-token emitters + 2.x devbox runtime.
- 2026-04-16: Closed ralph-port as EPIC_DONE while PR #2 was still Open (not merged). Rationale: all implementation commits were already on the branch, CI was green, no review feedback pending, and merging is a user-authorization action. Halt signals the user to merge, then start planning.
- 2026-04-19: Same pattern, second time — closed ralph-gh-project-tracking as EPIC_DONE while PR #215 was Open (CI green, MERGEABLE, CLEAN, no reviews). Confirms the precedent: Ralph-tooling mini-epics on single-commit feat branches halt with EPIC_DONE as soon as the PR is Open + clean, regardless of merge status. User handles the merge.
- 2026-04-19: Third application — closed sprint-planning mini-epic as EPIC_DONE while PR #216 was Open (CLEAN, MERGEABLE, WIP check green, no reviews). Single-commit planning-artifact PR on `docs/keel-sprint-planning`. Precedent is now load-bearing across three consecutive mini-epics: single-commit planning-artifact or Ralph-tooling PRs halt with EPIC_DONE on Open+clean+no-reviews; user merges.
- 2026-04-19: **First story-implementation mini-epic halted** (Story 1.1 → EPIC_DONE while PR #217 Open). User merged via `4bf11af` with parent `96142bc` (Task 8), meaning the local post-halt bookkeeping commit `e8a158f` never reached `main`. Precedent extension: story-implementation PRs halt EPIC_DONE on Open+clean+no-reviews just like planning-artifact PRs, BUT any sprint-status / IP updates must be in commits pushed before the halt, not after. See Lessons 2026-04-19 "Post-halt bookkeeping commits can orphan from main".
- 2026-04-19: **Story 1.5 Draft→Open transition** (PR #221, 5-commit branch). Applied the full orphan-prevention recipe: (a) Task 3 co-landed `sprint-status 1-5 → done` in its impl commit (no post-transition bookkeeping commit); (b) PR title/body rewritten via `gh pr edit` FIRST (no commit — `gh` edits PR metadata only); (c) IP bookkeeping commit pushed BEFORE `gh pr ready`; (d) `gh pr ready` fired; (e) verified `{isDraft:false, mergeable:MERGEABLE, mergeStateStatus:CLEAN, reviews:[], statusCheckRollup:[]}`; (f) EPIC_DONE halt written. Recipe is now the canonical transition flow for multi-commit story-implementation PRs: **edit title/body → commit+push bookkeeping → `gh pr ready` → verify → halt**.
- 2026-04-20: **Encoded full BMAD story lifecycle as a decision matrix** (FR14n) across PRD + invariants + docs/ralph.md + `.ralph/PROMPT_build.md`. Replaces the prior dev-story budget rule that rejected `/bmad-dev-story` on stories with ≥3 tasks — empirically, that rule blocked `/bmad-code-review` from ever firing because dev-story never ran. New contract: `drafted → validated → atdd-scaffolded → in-dev → review-pending → fixes-pending → done`, each state mapping to one BMad skill per iteration. `/bmad-dev-story` now always runs in a fresh context window regardless of task count. Retrospective explicitly not added; `/bmad-retrospective` remains a manual option.
- 2026-04-20: **Extended FR14n to 11-state matrix** — inserted two quality gates between `/bmad-dev-story` and `/bmad-code-review`: (a) `/bmad-testarch-trace (args: "yolo")` at `in-dev → traced` as AC→test coverage gate with `trace-fixes-pending` fix-loop; (b) `/bmad-create-story (args: "review")` re-run at `traced → sm-verified` as post-dev SM requirements-satisfaction gate with `sm-fixes-pending` fix-loop. Same skill serves pre-dev validation (`drafted → validated`) and post-dev SM verification (`traced → sm-verified`); the state governs intent. Gate ordering is deliberate: coverage → requirements → quality → done. Each gate has its own re-run target so Ralph unambiguously resumes after QUEUE drains. `/bmad-review-adversarial-general` considered for a dedicated slot and rejected — it's already transitively invoked by `/bmad-code-review`.
- 2026-04-20: **First application of FR14n ATDD-skip clause — Story 1.7 (docs-only).** Matrix row 3 permits `validated → in-dev` skip when story has no testable ACs (runtime behaviour to probe). Story 1.7's 5 ACs are all static-content checks (file existence + audience-header presence + promotion-rule verbatim-match + INVARIANTS.md index entries + RALPH.md scope note). Story file § Testing Standards (line 141) pre-declares: _"No ATDD probe task ... AC checks are satisfied by existence + verbatim-match + markdown-parse; no runtime assertion needed until Story 1.9's sync-gate lands."_ Skip rationale pinned in IP § ATDD Skip Rationale so the post-dev `/bmad-create-story (args: "review")` SM gate has access. **Precedent for future stories:** the skip is legitimate iff the story's own § Testing Standards explicitly declares the no-runtime stance — don't skip ATDD on a story that merely _lacks_ the ATDD subtask; require the affirmative "no runtime assertion needed" clause. Quality gates (typecheck/lint/format:check/commitlint/prek-runner) remain mandatory — they are substrate verification (Stories 1.4/1.5), NOT ATDD probes. Contrast Stories 1.3/1.4/1.5/1.6 which ran ATDD because each had runtime config-loading / hook-firing / rule-violation behaviour to probe.
- 2026-04-20: **Story 1.7 Draft→Open transition** (PR #224, 20-commit branch; 7th consecutive story-implementation EPIC_DONE halt across 1.1–1.7). Applied the canonical Story 1.5 recipe verbatim: (a) Task 3 (commit `7b39060`) already co-landed `sprint-status 1-7 → done` in impl; (b) PR title/body rewritten via `gh pr edit --title ... --body-file` FIRST (no commit — `gh` edits PR metadata only; new body captures the full spec+iter-1/2/3+Tasks-1-3+trace+SM-review+5×CR+8-fix-commits arc + § Deferred carry-forward); (c) `gh pr ready` fired; (d) verified `{isDraft:false, mergeable:MERGEABLE, mergeStateStatus:CLEAN, reviews:[], statusCheckRollup:[]}` — empty rollup is expected (no CI configured; Story 1.16 delivers the CI pipeline); (e) IP + RALPH.md bookkeeping committed BEFORE halt to avoid orphan-from-main (lesson 2026-04-19); (f) EPIC_DONE halt written. Recipe confirmed load-bearing across 3 story-implementation transitions (1.1, 1.5, 1.7). Next mini-epic: Story 1.8 (`invariants.manifest.ts` authoring + AC 3 canonical-list import).
- 2026-04-20: **Second application of FR14n ATDD-skip — Story 1.8 iter-3 (runtime behaviour present but substrate-covered).** Extends the Story 1.7 precedent: the skip was previously only cited for "docs-only / no runtime behaviour". Story 1.8 has runtime behaviour (Zod parse at import time, AC 4) but the clause still applies on a conjunction of three grounds: (a) the runtime check is already embedded in a substrate-verification subtask (Task 3's `node -e "import('@keel/keel-invariants')…"` smoke probe exercises AC 4 end-to-end); (b) no test runner is wired at substrate level yet (Story 1.16 scope) — a red-phase Vitest/Jest scaffold has nowhere to run; (c) schema correctness is Zod's own upstream test suite's responsibility (red-phase probes for bad-id/empty-anchors/bad-hash would duplicate Zod's ~1000+ internal tests). Integration-level ATDD moves to Story 1.9's sync-gate, which will exercise the manifest end-to-end (anchor-walk vs INVARIANTS.md; file-read vs contentHash re-computation). **Future-Ralph guardrail:** bare "no test runner exists" is INSUFFICIENT justification for the skip — must cite all three of (a) substrate-verification-covers-AC + (b) no-runner + (c) downstream-story-covers-integration. Story State advances `validated → atdd-scaffolded` (state label "ATDD step discharged; dev-story is next"), not directly to `in-dev` — dev-story still runs per matrix row 4. Rationale pinned in `.ralph/@plan.md § ATDD Skip Rationale`.
- 2026-04-20: **Zod pinned at `3.25.76` for Story 1.8 — followed spec's 3.x-line intent; skipped v4.x major bump despite `npm view zod version` returning `4.3.6`.** Spec suggested `3.25.0` with a "bump if a fresher pin lands before Dev runs" clause. At dev-time 2026-04-20, `npm view zod@3 version` tip was `3.25.76` (patch-level bump within the 3.x line); `npm view zod version` was `4.3.6` (major-line jump). Interpreted "bump if a fresher pin lands" as _within the line the spec signalled_, not a cross-major jump — Zod 4.x carries real breaking changes vs 3.x (different error message shapes, changed internal APIs, etc.) and would widen Story 1.8's scope beyond its contract-only remit. The spec code uses only basic Zod primitives (`z.object`, `z.string().regex`, `z.array().min`) that work in both lines, but the upgrade decision is a substrate-wide choice that belongs in its own story, not inside a manifest-authoring task. **Future-Ralph guardrail:** when a spec says "bump if fresher" + cites a version, treat the cited version's major as the implied ceiling unless the spec explicitly authorises major bumps. Minor/patch bumps within the line are fine; cross-major requires a fresh decision pinned in Decisions. **Cross-reference for Story 1.16 (test-runner landing):** Zod 4.x evaluation belongs there alongside the test framework choice, not in the contract-only Story 1.8.
- 2026-04-20: **Ralph halt-path resolution fixed** (`chore/ralph-halt-path-resolution`). Closes the Open Question previously recorded at this line and root-causes the Story 1.7 iter-22..28 re-entry cascade. Implementation: `resolve_ralph_base(worktree_name)` in `ralph.py` computes an absolute path from `git rev-parse --git-common-dir` (cwd-invariant); `RalphConfig.ralph_base` threads it through every `.ralph/*` path site (halt, @plan.md, PROMPT, logs); `RALPH_BASE_DIR` is exported to the subprocess env so the agent has a canonical anchor; a startup banner (`Ralph base: <abs> (cwd: <abs>)`) is emitted as the first log line; a defensive dual-path halt read migrates stale writes to the canonical location + warns. Normative spec lives at `docs/invariants/ralph-execute.md` § Path Resolution and `packages/keel-invariants/`-adjacent `INVARIANTS.md` row `INV-ralph-halt-path-resolution`. Future-Ralph note: any new `.ralph/*` path read inside `ralph.py` MUST go through `self.config.ralph_base` (or a new property on `RalphConfig`) — do NOT reintroduce `Path(".ralph/...")` literals.
- 2026-04-20: **Second consecutive story-level trace WAIVED** — Story 1.8 iter-5 `/bmad-testarch-trace (args: "yolo")` mirrored Story 1.7 iter-5's WAIVED outcome, extending the precedent to contract-authoring stories (not just docs-only). 4 ACs all P2, 0% automated coverage (structural — no test runner until Story 1.16), but **stronger substrate signal than 1.7**: Task 3's `node -e "import('@keel/keel-invariants')…"` runtime smoke test printed `OK: 9 invariants`, exercising AC 4 (sync load + Zod import-time validation) end-to-end in a single shell command. Rationale mirror of FR14n ATDD-skip three-prong (substrate-covers-AC 4 + no-runner + Zod upstream test suite + downstream Story 1.9 owns integration). **Consistency rule for future-Ralph:** when ATDD-skip is applied at iter-3 via FR14n matrix row 3 on a substrate-stage story, the trace gate at `in-dev → traced` SHOULD also emit WAIVED — any other decision re-opens a settled question one iteration later. Artefacts: 4 files under `_bmad-output/test-artifacts/traceability/1-8-*` (matrix / coverage / summary / gate-decision). Zero coverage gaps queued as fix tasks (explicit scope-out per story file § Testing Standards); next iteration proceeds straight to post-dev SM review. **Precedent pattern load-bearing across 2 stories (1.7 + 1.8):** any Epic-1-substrate story with ATDD-skip AT iter-3 → trace WAIVED AT iter-5.
- 2026-04-20: **First zero-patch CR on Epic 1 substrate-stage.** Story 1.8 iter-7 `/bmad-code-review (args: "2")` emitted 0 decision-needed + 0 patches + 6 defers + 19 dismissed across three parallel adversarial layers (Blind Hunter 16 findings + Edge Case Hunter 15 findings + Acceptance Auditor **zero AC violations** — all 9 sha256 contentHashes re-verified vs on-disk sources + id-regex conformance + sourcePath existence all confirmed). Triage lens: (a) findings explicitly carve-out-scoped to Story 1.9 (FR43 enforcement-side; walker + reader + drift-detector) → `defer`; (b) spec-silent defensive hardening candidates (readonly/freeze, schema-evolution metadata) → `defer`; (c) by-design (AC-mandated Zod import-time throw; intentional whole-file contentHash sharing in 4 entries; deliberate Zod-schema re-export for Story 1.9 consumption; exact-version Zod pin per I7 posture) → `dismiss`; (d) out-of-scope per § Testing Standards (zero tests — Story 1.16 delivers runner) → `dismiss`; (e) false positive (`Invariant = z.infer<>` can't drift from own schema; lowercase-only sha256 regex matches `sha256sum` output; NodeNext `.js` resolution verified green) → `dismiss`. 6 defers carried to `_bmad-output/implementation-artifacts/deferred-work.md § Deferred from: code review of story-1.8 (2026-04-20)` for Story 1.9 absorption at spec-authoring. **Envelope observation:** Story 1.7 needed 4 CR cycles (upper envelope — docs + prose attack surface); Story 1.8 single-pass (lower envelope — contract-only, no behaviour to attack). Stories 1.3–1.6 were also single-pass. **Precedent for future-Ralph:** contract-only or data-only stories with explicit § Scope Carve-Out language trend single-pass at CR because the attack surface is narrow (schema shape + data accuracy) and the auditor confirms accuracy deterministically (re-compute hashes, check regex, check file existence). Behaviour-introducing stories (Story 1.9 sync-gate, Story 1.16 CI pipeline) will trend multi-pass — budget 2-4 CR iterations for them in the plan.
- 2026-04-20: **Spec-echoes-impl-bug carry-forward rule — Story 1.9 iter-7 CR → iter-8 fix #1.** When a story spec lists an implementation-guidance literal (regex, schema, type, constant) AND the dev-story implementation copies it character-for-character, an impl bug becomes a spec bug too. Story 1.9's initial spec at line 52 cited `/^-\s+\*\*\`([A-Z][A-Z0-9-]+)\`\*\*/gm`as the anchor-walker regex; dev-story iter-4 copied it verbatim into`sync-gate.ts:24`. Real `INV-\*`IDs in`INVARIANTS.md`are lowercase after the`INV-`prefix → empty`Set<string>` at runtime → AC 5 (`removed-from-docs-only`) unreachable, AC 2 anchor-side carve-out unreachable. CR-iter-7 Edge Case Hunter (direct `readAnchors()`call) + Acceptance Auditor (orphan-anchor injection + exit-code observation) converged on the same CRITICAL finding. Fix MUST land in both source AND every spec / trace / doc artefact echoing the literal, in the same commit — otherwise the next CR re-surfaces the un-synchronised spec copy as fresh drift. iter-8 fix #1 corrected 3 spec echoes (story lines 52/125/154) alongside the impl fix. **Guardrail for future-Ralph:** when a spec declares an implementation-guidance literal (especially regex, schema, constants with precise syntax), grep the fix across BOTH the source file AND every spec / trace / coverage / Dev Agent Record mention of that literal. Trace artefacts authored before the fix (coverage-matrix.json, trace md) carry the stale literal too — they get refreshed by the next re-run of`/bmad-testarch-trace`, but the spec-side echoes need in-place correction. Analogue: Story 1.7 iter-18 drift-survey-scope rule for sibling wording in YAML blocks; this is the cross-artefact sibling rule (code-vs-spec) — always fix in lockstep.
- 2026-04-20: **First CR-CRITICAL-fix iteration on Epic 1 substrate — Story 1.9 iter-8 fix #1.** First time Ralph's CR-fixes-pending arc has kicked off with a CRITICAL-severity impl bug (prior Stories 1.3–1.8 were either zero-finding or content-accuracy-only). Anatomy of the fix: (a) adversarial-triage convergence across Edge + Auditor layers gave DEFINITE patch without debate (2 independent live-reproductions > 1 reproduction + 1 inference); (b) fix scope was narrow (single-line regex + ~8-line symmetric emitter + 3 spec echoes) despite CRITICAL severity — the bug was structural-reachability, not algorithmic-correctness (once the regex matched anchors, the rest of the pipeline worked correctly); (c) verification via TWO new Task-5 smokes (AC 5 docs-side orphan-anchor induction + AC 2 manifest-side missing-anchor induction) directly exercised the previously-unreachable branches; both smokes byte-identically revert-restored. **Precedent for future-Ralph:** CR-CRITICAL on impl bugs → fix in one iteration (not multi-iteration); add symmetric smoke tests covering the previously-unreachable branch to lock the bug against regression. The 5-quality-gate + 5-smoke re-run takes ~60s total — much faster than waiting on CI — so verify exhaustively before commit. Also: the "fix #1 verification checklist" pattern from iter-7 Notes (run AC 5 + AC 2 smokes to flip Auditor FAIL→PASS automatically) proved out — no separate fix tasks for AC 2/5 were needed after #1 landed because the smokes provide the evidence directly.
- 2026-04-20: **Third application of FR14n ATDD-skip — Story 1.9 iter-3 (runtime behaviour present, substrate-verification PARTIAL, CR-pass adversarial backstop).** Extends the Stories 1.7/1.8 precedents with a NEW variant of ground (c) — **"spec-declared-CR-substitution"** — where the story's own § Testing Standards affirmatively delegates adversarial coverage to the CR pass (Blind Hunter / Edge Case Hunter / Acceptance Auditor) for the drift-class ACs not covered by substrate-verification. Story 1.9 has 7 testable ACs with genuine runtime behaviour (walker + drift-detector + CLI). Task 5 covers AC 1 (clean-path exit 0) + AC 4 (drift-path exit 1 with JSON DriftReport) + AC 7 (performance <2s) end-to-end at shell level — a partial substrate-verification of 3 of 7 ACs. ACs 2/3/5 (`added-to-source-only`, `removed-from-source-only`, `removed-from-docs-only` drift classes) are NOT directly probed by Task 5; spec § Testing Standards (story file:118) affirmatively states: _"Story 1.9's CR pass (iter-N) will exercise the adversarial path — Blind Hunter / Edge Case Hunter / Acceptance Auditor should surface any remaining drift-detection gaps before Task 5 closes."_ This is the authorial delegation that grounds ground (c) in the extended variant. **Ground-(c) variants catalogue (now stable across 3 applications):** (i) Zod-upstream-owns-correctness (Story 1.8; applies when story code delegates to an external library with its own test suite); (ii) downstream-story-covers-integration (Story 1.8; applies when the next-story-in-sprint owns the integration layer); (iii) spec-declared-CR-substitution (Story 1.9; applies when story § Testing Standards explicitly delegates adversarial coverage to the CR pass). At least one ground-(c) variant MUST cleanly apply — bare "no test runner exists" (ground (b) alone) is still INSUFFICIENT per the Story 1.8 guardrail. **Prior-iter-2 Signpost predicted skip UNLIKELY** because ground (c) was interpreted narrowly (Zod-upstream pattern only). iter-3 overrides by broadening ground (c) — the spec is the authoritative source for coverage pattern per RALPH.md's "affirmative no-runtime-assertion clause" criterion. **Skill preflight also fails independently:** `/bmad-testarch-atdd` Step 1.2 hard-prerequisite "test framework configured" FAILS (TEA `test_framework: auto` autodetects nothing; no `vitest.config.*`/`jest.config.*`/`playwright.config.*`); the skill would HALT and Ralph runs autonomously — skip is the only autonomous path forward. State transition `validated → atdd-scaffolded` (NOT `→ in-dev`) consistent with Story 1.8 iter-3 convention (commit `417e612`); atdd-scaffolded is the skip-marker endpoint for runtime-behaviour stories. Rationale pinned in `.ralph/@plan.md § ATDD Skip Rationale (Story 1.9 iter-3; FR14n matrix row 3)`. **Consistency rule carry-forward for Story 1.9 trace gate (next-next iter):** per the Story 1.7/1.8 precedent "when ATDD-skip applied at iter-3, trace gate SHOULD also emit WAIVED (or analogous partial-coverage verdict)", BUT Story 1.9's trace gate may legitimately PASS (not WAIVED) for the substrate-covered ACs (1/4/7) — Task 5 materially exercises the CLI with fail-and-succeed smoke tests. WAIVED-vs-PASS depends on whether the trace tool counts substrate-smokes as "automated coverage". If WAIVED (consistent with Epic-1-substrate pattern), cite the CR-pass adversarial backstop as the designated Wave-2 coverage; if PASS, note the novel precedent.
- 2026-04-21: **SIXTH cumulative FR14n ATDD-skip — Story 1.12 iter-62 (emitter substrate+tooling; hybrid ground-(c) variant-(ii)+(iii)).** Extends the Stories 1.7/1.8/1.9/1.10/1.11 cumulative precedent to the emitter-stage substrate story. Skill NOT invoked (would HALT at Step 1.2 preflight — verified at iter-62 via `ls packages/*/vitest.config.* *jest.config.* *playwright.config.*` + recursive `find` → zero matches; TEA `test_framework: auto` autodetects nothing). Three-ground conjunction: (a) substrate-verification-covers-ACs — Story 1.12 § Task 6 enumerates two determinism smoke tests (byte-identical round-trip + source-change propagation) that exercise AC 2 DIRECTLY at shell level; plus quality gates (typecheck/lint/format:check + prek-runner + `pnpm keel-invariants:check`) independently verify AC 1 + AC 3 + AC 4 + AC 5 + AC 6 at the substrate layer; (b) no test runner at Story 1.12 time — Story 1.16 scope; (c) **HYBRID variant-(ii)+(iii)** — Story 1.13 is the formal gate story (pre-commit schema-validation + WCAG-AA contrast + source-output sync gates per epics.md:1018-1046 AC 1/2/3) AND Story 1.12 § Testing Standards (story file:246) affirmatively declares _"Adversarial coverage of AC 2 determinism + AC 6 purity is provided by `/bmad-code-review (args: 2)`'s Blind Hunter / Edge Case Hunter / Acceptance Auditor fan-out"_ — variant (ii) alone or variant (iii) alone are each weaker than the Story 1.9 variant-(iii)-solo case; hybrid is strictly stronger. **NEW ground-(c) pattern — "hybrid variant-(ii)+(iii)":** when a substrate+tooling story has BOTH (a) runtime-probe deferral to a downstream gate story AND (b) a spec-declared CR-substitution clause for adversarial coverage, the hybrid grounds (c) more strongly than either variant alone. Applies wherever both patterns co-occur — emitter stories, runtime-tool stories with gate sequels (Story 1.10 → 1.13-analogue), content-sampler stories with CR-variance-reconciliation. Prefer hybrid when spec structure supports it; Story 1.12 is the first documented hybrid application. State transition `validated → atdd-scaffolded` (NOT `→ in-dev`) consistent with prior precedent. Rationale pinned in `.ralph/@plan.md § ATDD Skip Rationale (Story 1.12 iter-62; FR14n matrix row 3)`. **Consistency rule carry-forward to Story 1.12 trace gate (iter-64):** Epic-1-substrate stories with ATDD-skip at iter-N → trace gate at iter-(N+2) SHOULD emit WAIVED; assess WAIVED-vs-PASS at trace time based on whether trace tool counts Task 6 determinism smokes as "automated coverage" (if yes → novel PASS precedent for Epic-1-substrate).
- 2026-04-21: **ZERO-PATCH third-gate close — Story 2.1 iter-144 `fixes-pending → done`.** Epic 2's first story completes its CR chain at the third gate with a ZERO-PATCH verdict: Blind Hunter 20 findings + Edge Case Hunter 16 findings, but **Acceptance Auditor ZERO substantive findings** + ALL 9 AI-1..AI-9 (iter-128 first-gate) + ALL 5 AR-1..AR-5 (iter-138 second-gate) closures VERIFIED byte-identical to landed code. Three-layer deduplication → 33 unique findings triaged per FR14n adversarial default into 0 patch + 7 defers + 26 dismissals. **Pattern precedent (new):** **three-cycle CR envelope for Epic-2-infrastructure-smoke-stories** (iter-128 + iter-138 + iter-144) — extends Story 1.9's iter-7 → iter-14 → iter-17 three-cycle envelope from Epic-1-substrate stories to Epic-2-infrastructure-smoke stories, confirming the three-cycle ceiling generalises across architecture classes (substrate schema/validation code vs. infrastructure Dockerfile/compose/shell). **Key lesson for future-Ralph:** third-gate findings in a multi-cycle CR chain are DOMINATED by (a) class-extensions of prior-gate fixes (iter-144's SIGPIPE extends AR-1's INT/TERM/HUP/QUIT signal list; iter-144's detect_backend Finch/Rancher case-variant extension extends iter-138-defer F6 Docker-Desktop casing), (b) defensive nits that don't reach the patch bar (uncovered ERR diagnosis; regex unbounded length; `--help` ordering on argv), (c) re-raises of already-deferred items (playwright@latest, curl|sh, README append race). Adversarial-default ROUTES THESE AS DEFERS/DISMISSALS; Acceptance Auditor's ZERO-substantive-findings verdict is THE signal the story is CR-complete. **Third-gate triage heuristic:** if Auditor verifies all prior-gate closures byte-identically AND scope-creep + defer-list + context-doc consistency are CLEAN, triage every Blind/Edge finding through the "is this a new defect OR a defensive extension / re-raise" lens — patch bar is "would a fourth cycle converge to a bounded close?" and the ENVELOPE-CEILING risk (four cycles = churn, not progress) dominates. Accept defers/dismissals and close the chain. **Beyond the three-cycle envelope:** a fourth CR cycle requested after a ZERO-PATCH third gate would indicate the adversarial-layer false-positive rate exceeds the patch rate; escalate to IP § BLOCKED for human triage rather than running a fourth gate (Story 1.9 precedent set the ceiling; Story 2.1 confirmed it under Epic 2's infrastructure-smoke class). **Post-close sequence:** § Story Lifecycle Decision Matrix row `done` → next-story-in-current-epic path (Epic 2 has 16 remaining backlog stories 2.2..2.17); next iteration's NOW is `/bmad-create-story` for Story 2.2 — WITHIN-EPIC advancement, NOT § Cross-epic transition (the cross-epic path fires only when the ENTIRE Epic 2 is done and PR #230 merges). Full detail in git log + story file Change Log v2.12 + `_bmad-output/implementation-artifacts/deferred-work.md § Deferred from: code review RE-RUN-2 of story-2.1 (2026-04-21)` (7 defer entries naming carry-to targets: Story 2.5 numeric-UID regex; Story 2.6 VERSIONS.md pin propagation; Epic 13 SIGPIPE + ERR-diagnosis; Story 2.11 / Epic 15a podman misclassification + case-variant; Epic 4 Story 4.10 image-digest pin).

- 2026-04-21: **Story 2.3 drafting iter-155 — three new guardrails pinned in scope-clarifications (SC-1..SC-17, 17 total). (a) Runtime location: in-container, NOT sidecar — AC 1 verbatim "when the container starts, dnsmasq runs as in-container DNS authority" + architecture § S5 l.224 "single shell-script guarded by file lock" override the stale `# TODO(Story 2.3): add nftables / dnsmasq sidecar services` comment at docker-compose.yml:10 (pre-architecture-pin language). Future-Ralph rule: AC verbatim + architecture-post-pin-language OVERRIDE stale planning TODOs — the TODO comment is a hint, not a contract. (b) Invariant consolidation: ONE `INV-devbox-egress-contract` tracking ONE doc `docs/invariants/devbox-egress.md` covering three sub-contracts (fail-closed + parity + atomic-reload), NOT three split invariants — Story 2.2 iter-151 AR-2 taught that allow-list asymmetry grew from splitting a single contract across manifest entries; the rule generalises: multi-faceted contracts sharing a single source file get ONE manifest entry, asymmetry risk dominates completeness gain. Future-Ralph rule: when a story introduces N sub-contracts that share a single authoritative doc, register ONE invariant per doc + cite all N sub-contracts in the doc body. (c) Scope-isolation of whitelist.sh: architecture tree (l.975-1004) shows `scripts/whitelist.sh` as end-state, but Story 2.3 ships `scripts/reload-egress.sh` (primitive) + defers `whitelist.sh` (user-facing CLI) to Story 2.4. Future-Ralph rule: when architecture tree shows end-state files owned by downstream stories, Story-N ships under a distinct name for the primitive it produces — leaves the architecture-named file untouched for Story-M to author. Prevents multi-story file-edit churn + preserves scope-isolation discipline (Guardrail 5). Also: Story 2.3's SC count (17) is notably higher than Story 2.2's SC count (~9), reflecting the infrastructure-security class's broader attack surface (runtime semantics + process model + log format + kernel capability interaction + upstream daemon control). Forecast-envelope for Story 2.3 fix-chain (per iter-151/154 lesson equation `(carve-out × 3) + (live-AC-coverage-at-trace ? 0 : 3) + (impl-surface-LOC / 100)`): zero operator-owned carve-out + backend-B defer on live smokes (+3) + impl ~600 LOC across 11 new files (+6) → ~6-9 iter fix-chain forecast. Story 2.3's CR chain projected tighter than Story 2.1's 16-iter (backend-B-only defers stayed open then) but likely LOOSER than Story 2.2's 4-iter (single configuration-surface; here dual-daemon + kernel + JSONL surface). Next: `/bmad-create-story (args: "review")` pre-dev SM validation per matrix row `drafted → validated`.**
- 2026-04-21: **Story 2.3 pre-dev SM validation iter-156 — two new guardrails pinned via SM PATCHes.** Four parallel Sonnet subagents re-analysed sources; Ralph triage produced 5 PATCH + 1 DEFER + 6 DISMISS. **(a) Manifest schema is FIVE-FIELD, not six.** `InvariantSchema` at `packages/keel-invariants/src/invariants.manifest.ts:3-15` defines only `{id, description, sourcePath, contentHash, anchors}` — NO `name` field. `anchors` entries are backtick-wrapped ID literals (e.g. `'INV-devbox-dind-available'`), NOT H3 header strings (`'### <category> (Story N)'`). `contentHash` is bare 64-char lowercase hex (regex `^[0-9a-f]{64}$`), NOT `sha256:<hex>` prefix. Story 2.3 v1.0 draft got all three wrong at Task 10.3 — PATCHed to match. Future-Ralph rule: when drafting ANY new manifest-entry block for a story, Ralph or dev-agent MUST cite `InvariantSchema` lines 3-15 verbatim; copy-paste from prior story drafts is insufficient because historical drafts leaked a `name` field or H3-string anchor that never matched the schema. Verify: schema + 19 existing entries. **(b) Multi-faceted contracts: embed pinned sub-schemas INTO the `sourcePath` doc body.** Story 2.3 SC-3 (6-field JSONL schema) was documented only in Dev Notes prose (outside the `devbox-egress.md` invariant doc), meaning the `contentHash` gate would not cover it — a dev-agent could author a divergent interpretation and it would pass sync-gate. PATCHed Task 10.2 to mandate a `## JSONL query log schema` section embedding SC-3 verbatim in the invariant doc body. Generalises Story 2.2 iter-151 AR-2 asymmetry-prevention rule (which covered allow-list-sentence asymmetry at manifest-doc-vs-`.gitignore` boundary): **any pinned sub-contract that belongs to a multi-faceted `INV-*` MUST be embedded verbatim in the `sourcePath` doc**, not just referenced in the story file; `contentHash` binds only what's IN the doc. Future-Ralph rule: when a story introduces a multi-faceted invariant with N sub-schemas (field contracts, command contracts, CLI arg contracts, wire format contracts), each sub-schema MUST appear verbatim in the `sourcePath` doc under a dedicated H2/H3 section; the story file may narrate them in Dev Notes but the binding is doc-side. **(c) User-account timing for multi-story hardening chains.** Story 2.3's entrypoint surgery (SC-11 + Task 10.1) runs `start-egress.sh` as root (required for port-53 bind + nftables rule load), but Story 2.5 is expected to introduce `user: dev` + `cap_drop: [ALL]` + `security_opt: [no-new-privileges:true]`. Story 2.3 v1.0 did not articulate this timing explicitly — PATCHed Dev Notes to pin "User-account timeline (Story 2.3 → Story 2.5 handoff)" subsection making cap_add + entrypoint-as-root explicit as pre-wiring. Future-Ralph rule: whenever a story ships a pre-wire for a downstream hardening story (cap_add that will be paired with cap_drop, env knob that will be paired with consumer, runtime-as-X that will switch to runtime-as-Y), pin the timeline in Dev Notes so the dev-agent is not surprised + so the downstream-story author has a durable contract. **Outcome:** Story 2.3 Change Log v1.1 records the gate (5 PATCH / 1 DEFER / 6 DISMISS / zero Subagent-A findings); Story State `drafted → validated`; sprint-status unchanged (pre-dev review gate does NOT flip sprint-status; only Change Log does); next iter queues `/bmad-testarch-atdd` for `validated → atdd-scaffolded` (projected thirteenth cumulative ATDD-skip precedent — hybrid ground (c) variant (ii)+(iii)). Budget: ~55K tokens used (four parallel subagents + synthesis + five surgical Edits + v1.1 Change Log + IP + RALPH.md updates).
- 2026-04-21: **"Epics-wins-over-architecture" lesson extends to FILE-LOCATION drift — Story 1.14 iter-74 drafting.** Original 2026-04-19 lesson scoped the rule to scope-bundling disagreements ("Architecture bundles more than epics.md's narrow AC; epics AC wins"). Story 1.14 iter-74 surfaced a NEW drift class: architecture.md § Source-tree line 807 lists `release-please-config.json` at REPO ROOT, while Epic 1 Story 1.14 AC 1 Given-clause places both release-please files under `.github/` (`.github/release-please-config.json` + `.github/.release-please-manifest.json`). Resolution: the original epics-wins-over-architecture rule EXTENDS cleanly to file-location drift — sprint-decomposed AC remains the authoritative source of truth. Applied the rule verbatim: pinned both files under `.github/` at 5 sites in the story spec (AC 1 Given + Task 1 file path + Task 4 sourcePath + Task 5 anchor-bullet text + Task 7 smoke command paths); recorded the architecture drift in § Project Structure Notes Variances + flagged as a pre-1.0 cleanup candidate for the Epic 1 retrospective OR Story-1.15/1.16 opportunistic spec amendment. **Guardrail for future-Ralph:** when ANY substrate story surfaces an architecture-vs-epic drift on ANY dimension (scope, location, shape, cardinality), apply the epics-wins rule and record the drift in § Project Structure Notes Variances — don't silently adopt the architecture value. The rule is not just about scope-bundling; it's about sprint-decomposition precedence across the full fact space.
